Refuting the Mu'tazilite Argument on Annihilation
Al-Taftazani refutes the Mu'tazilite argument on annihilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani refutes the Mu'tazilite argument that annihilation is purposeless, and why God's purposes are not limited to human benefit or recompense.

Core Idea
God's actions are never futile, even if we cannot grasp their purpose.

The Mu'tazilites argued that since God is wise, His actions must have a purpose; annihilation, they claimed, has no purpose because it benefits no one. In this passage, al-Taftazani refutes this by broadening the concept of purpose beyond mere benefit and recompense, and by showing that even the announcement of annihilation serves divine wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite argument
Start by reading the Mu'tazilite claim that God's actions must have a purpose, and that annihilation lacks purpose because it provides no benefit and is not a recompense.
Notice how they equate purpose with benefit and recompense.
2
Identify the refutation
Find where al-Taftazani denies that purpose is limited to benefit and recompense, and where he suggests hidden wisdoms known only to God.
3
Examine the additional points
Look at the points about luṭf (kindness) and manifestation of God's majesty and self-sufficiency.
Announcement of annihilation itself serves a purpose.
4
Analyze the separation of parts objection
Read the objection about how dispersed parts might prevent restoration, and note the distinction between atoms and attributes.
5
Understand the analogy
Consider the analogy of a criminal who changes physically but remains the same person for retribution.
This illustrates that the underlying essence persists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - وهو للمعتزلة أن فعل الحكيم لا بد أن يكون لغرض لامتناع العبث عليه، ولا يتصور له غرض في الإعدام إذ لا منفعة فيه لأحد، لأنها إنما تكون مع الوجود، بل الحياة. وليس ايضاً جزاء المستحق كالعذاب والسؤال والحساب، ونحو ذلك، وهذا ظاهر. ورد بمنع انحصار الغرض في المنفعة والجزاء، فلعل الله تعالى في ذلك حكماً ومصالح لا يعلمها غيره على أن في الإخبار بالإعدام لطفاً للمكلفين، وإظهاراً لغاية العظمة والاستغناء، والتفرد بالدوام والبقاء، ثم الإعدام تحقيق لذلك وتصديق، وقد يورد الوجهان على طريق تفريق الأجزاء، أما الثاني فظاهر، وأما الأول فلانعدام التأليف والهيئات التي بها التمايز. فإما أن تمتنع الإعادة، أو يلتبس المعاد بالمثل ويجاب بأنه يجوز أن لا تنعدم الصفات التي بها التمايز كاختصاص الجواهر بما لها من الجهات مثلاً، ولو سلم فالمستحق هو تلك الجواهر الموصوفة الباقية لا مجموع الجواهر والصفات والتعينات، كما إذا جنى وهو شاب سمين سليم الأعضاء، واقتص منه حين صار هرماً عجيفاً ساقط الأعضاء، وعن الثاني بأن في التفريق منفعة الاعتبار، وإمكان اللذة والألم على طريق الجزاء.
The second: it is for the Mu'tazila that the action of the wise must be for a purpose because futility is impossible for Him, and no purpose is conceivable for Him in annihilation since there is no benefit in it for anyone, because benefit only occurs with existence, rather with life. And it is also not a recompense of the deserving like punishment, questioning, reckoning, and the like, and this is apparent. It is refuted by denying that purpose is limited to benefit and recompense; perhaps God has in that wisdoms and interests that none other than Him knows, besides that in the announcement of annihilation there is a kindness (luṭf) for the obligated, and a manifestation of utmost majesty and self-sufficiency, and uniqueness in perpetuity and permanence, then annihilation is a realization and confirmation of that. And the two aspects may be advanced concerning the way of separation of parts: as for the second, it is apparent; as for the first, it is due to the non-annihilation of the composition and forms by which differentiation occurs. So either restoration is impossible, or the restored one becomes confused with the similar. And it is answered that it is permissible that the attributes by which differentiation occurs do not cease to exist, like the specification of atoms with their directions for example. And even if conceded, the deserving entity is those remaining described atoms, not the aggregate of atoms, attributes, and particularizations, as when one commits a crime while young, fat, with sound limbs, and retaliation is exacted from him when he has become old, weak, and lost limbs. And concerning the second, that in the separation there is a benefit of consideration and the possibility of pleasure and pain by way of recompense.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage refutes the second argument of the Mu'tazila against the resurrection of bodies from annihilation. The Mu'tazila argue that God, being wise, must act for a purpose; annihilation has no purpose because it provides no benefit to anyone and is not a recompense. The author refutes this by denying that purpose is limited to benefit and recompense; God may have hidden wisdoms. He also notes that the announcement of annihilation itself serves as a kindness (luṭf) to the obligated and manifests God's majesty. Then the author addresses a potential objection about the separation of parts: if the body's parts are dispersed, how can the same person be restored? He answers that the underlying atoms (jawāhir) and certain differentiating attributes (like spatial relations) may persist, so the same person is restored. He uses an analogy of a criminal who changes in body but is still the same person. The second aspect—that separation itself has benefits—is also answered.

Key Terms
الإعدام
الغرض
العبث
اللطف
تفريق الأجزاء
التمايز
الجواهر
الإعادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Annihilation is pointless because it provides no benefit to anyone.
Correction: God's purposes are not limited to benefit and recompense; He has hidden wisdoms, and annihilation manifests His majesty and serves as confirmation of His announcement.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does the author refute the Mu'tazilite claim that annihilation is purposeless?
A) By arguing that annihilation does provide benefit to the deceased.
B) By denying that purpose is limited to benefit and recompense, and suggesting hidden wisdoms.
C) By claiming that the Mu'tazila are not qualified to speak on this matter.
D) By quoting verses that explicitly mention annihilation.

Key Takeaway
God's actions are always wise, even if we cannot comprehend their purposes; annihilation serves divine wisdom beyond human benefit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at events in your life that seem pointless or even unjust, do you truly believe that God has a wisdom you cannot see, or do you secretly expect everything to make sense to you? And what must you change about your trust in Him today?
?
The passage says that even the announcement of annihilation is a kindness from God. Can you recall a time when something God announced or commanded initially seemed harsh or unnecessary to you, but later you saw it as a mercy? How does that memory challenge you to submit to His word before understanding it?
?
If you were to stand before God tomorrow and He asked you, 'Did you trust My wisdom when you could not see My purpose?', would you have an answer? What one concrete step will you take this week to surrender your need to fully understand His decree?

Refuting the Scriptural Claim for Resurrection without Annihilation
Al-Taftazani refutes the scriptural argument for resurrection without annihilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani refutes the claim that Quranic verses prove resurrection without prior annihilation, showing that these verses do not negate annihilation and are counterbalanced by other verses.

Core Idea
Resurrection verses describe how, not whether – they don't deny annihilation.

Some argue that Quranic descriptions of resurrection as reviving the dead and gathering scattered parts imply the body is never annihilated. In this passage, al-Taftazani responds to this scriptural argument, explaining that such verses are about the manner of resurrection, not a denial of annihilation, and that other verses indicate annihilation. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponents' scriptural evidence
Read the list of Quranic verses cited by those who claim resurrection is by reviving after death without annihilation. Notice the pattern: they emphasize gathering and reviving.
2
Identify the two-part answer
Al-Taftazani gives a two-part answer: first, these verses do not negate annihilation; second, they were revealed to explain the manner of resurrection because the context required it.
3
Understand the counterbalance
He then notes that these verses are counterbalanced by other verses that clearly indicate annihilation and perishing. This shows the evidence is not one-sided.
This demonstrates the principle that conflicting scriptural evidence must be reconciled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث - النصوص الدالة على كون النشور بالإحياء بعد الموت، والجمع بعد التفرق لا الإيجاد، وبعد العدم كقوله تعالى : ( وإذ قال إبراهيم رب أرني كيف تحيي الموتى ) الآية وكقوله : ( أو كالذي مر على قرية ) إلى قوله : ثم نكسوها لحماً). وكقوله : ( كذلك المنشور ) ( كذلك تخرجون ) وكما بدأكم تعودون)؟ بعدما ذكر بدء الخلق من طين على وجه يرى ويشاهد مثل : ( أو لم يروا كيف يبدأ الله الخلق ) . قل سيروا في الأرض فانظروا كيف بدأ الخلق) :وكقوله : ( يوم يكون الناس كالفراش المبثوث وتكون الجبال كالعهن المنفوش ) إلى غير ذلك من الآيات المشعرة بالتفريق دون الإعدام. والجواب - أنها لا تنفي الإعدام، وإن لم تدل عليه . وإنما سيقت بياناً لكيفية الإحياء بعد الموت. والجمع بعد التفريق لأن السؤال وقع عن ذلك، ولأنه أظهر في بادىء النظر، والشواهد عليه أكثر ، ثم هي معارضة بما سبق من الآيات المشعرة بالإعدام والفناء.
The third: the texts indicating that resurrection is by reviving after death, and gathering after dispersion, not by origination, and after non-existence, like His saying: 'And when Abraham said, My Lord, show me how You give life to the dead' (Q2:260) and His saying: 'Or like the one who passed by a town' (Q2:259) until His saying: 'Then We clothed them with flesh' (Q2:259). And His saying: 'Thus is the resurrection' (Q35:9), 'Thus you will be brought forth' (Q30:19), 'And as He began you, you will return' (Q7:29), after mentioning the beginning of creation from clay in a manner seen and witnessed, like: 'Have they not seen how Allah begins creation?' (Q29:19), 'Say, travel through the earth and see how He began creation' (Q29:20), and His saying: 'The Day when people will be like scattered moths and the mountains will be like carded wool' (Q101:4-5), and other verses indicating dispersion without annihilation. The answer: they do not negate annihilation, even if they do not indicate it. They were only brought to explain the manner of reviving after death and gathering after dispersion, because the question was about that, and because it is more apparent at first glance and there are more evidences for it, and then they are counterbalanced by previous verses indicating annihilation and perishing.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument of the opponents (likely the Mu'tazila or Dahriyya) who cite scriptural verses that describe resurrection as a reviving after death and gathering after dispersion, implying that the body is not annihilated but merely separated. The author responds that these verses do not deny annihilation; they are only describing the manner of revival because that was the context of the question. Moreover, these verses are counterbalanced by other verses that explicitly speak of annihilation and perishing. The point is that the scriptural evidence does not decisively support the denial of annihilation.

Key Terms
النشور
الإحياء
الإعدام
التفريق
الآيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Quranic verses about resurrection (e.g., reviving the dead, gathering scattered parts) prove that the body is not annihilated and that resurrection is merely reassembly.
Correction: These verses do not deny annihilation; they address the manner of resurrection in response to specific questions, and they are counterbalanced by other verses that speak of annihilation.

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the scriptural evidence that resurrection involves reviving after death and gathering after dispersion?
A) He accepts that these verses prove the body is never annihilated.
B) He argues that the verses are allegorical and not to be taken literally.
C) He says the verses do not negate annihilation, and are counterbalanced by other verses.
D) He claims the verses were abrogated by later revelations.

Key Takeaway
Scriptural verses about resurrection describe its manner and do not exclude annihilation; they are counterbalanced by other verses that speak of annihilation and perishing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses describing resurrection, do you automatically assume they tell the whole story? What other verses might you be ignoring that speak of annihilation, and how will you commit to reading the Quran holistically, not cherry-picking?
?
How often do you cling to an initial understanding of a few verses, refusing to let other clear verses challenge your view? When was the last time you changed a deeply held belief after seeing the full scriptural picture?
?
If the resurrection involves complete annihilation of your body and then a new creation, does that change how you think about your own death? Are you truly prepared to be dissolved into nothingness before being recreated by Allah? What tangible step will you take this week to live with that reality?

Paradise and Hell are Created Now: Evidence and First Objection
Al-Taftazani affirms Paradise and Hell are created now against some Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural evidence for the Sunni position that Paradise and Hell currently exist, and the first objection from those who deny this.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell exist now, not just in the future.

Al-Taftazani opens this research topic by firmly stating that Paradise and Hell are already created. He supports this with clear Quranic verses and the story of Adam and Eve. He then addresses the first objection from the Mu'tazila, who argue that creating them before Judgment Day is futile, but notes its weakness.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style of Al-Taftazani.
2
Identify the main claim and evidence
Identify the central assertion and the three pieces of evidence: the story of Adam and Eve, the Quranic verses with 'prepared', and the verses about bringing near.
The past tense 'prepared' indicates prior existence.
3
Understand the dismissal of metaphorical interpretation
Note how Al-Taftazani rejects metaphorical readings as departing from the apparent meaning without proof.
This is a key methodological point in kalam.
4
Analyze the first objection and its refutation
Read the objection that creation before Judgment Day is futile, and notice that Al-Taftazani simply states its weakness is apparent, implying a rational argument.
Think about why futility might be argued and why it fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الخامس - الجنة والنار مخلوقتان الآن خلافاً لبعض المعتزلة لنا قصة آدم وحواء، والنصوص الشاهدة بذلك مثل : أعدت للمتقين أعدت للكافرين ( وأزلفت الجنة للمتقين، وبرزت الجحيم للغاوين) وحملها على المجاز عدول عن الظاهر بلا دليل . احتج المنكرون بوجوه الأول - أن خلقهما قبل يوم الجزاء عبث، وضعفه ظاهر.
He said: The fifth research topic: Paradise and Hell are created now, contrary to some Mu'tazila. For us is the story of Adam and Eve, and the texts witnessing to that, such as: 'Prepared for the righteous' (Q3:133), 'Prepared for the disbelievers' (Q2:24), and 'And Paradise will be brought near to the righteous, and Hell will be exposed for the deviators' (Q26:90-91). And interpreting them metaphorically is a departure from the apparent meaning without evidence. The deniers argued with proofs: The first: that creating them before the Day of Recompense is futile, and its weakness is apparent.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage introduces the fifth research topic (al-mabḥath al-khāmis) of the chapter. The author asserts that Paradise and Hell are already created and currently exist. This is contrary to the view of some Mu'tazila. The evidence includes the story of Adam and Eve (implying Paradise existed) and explicit Quranic verses that use the past tense 'prepared' (uʿiddat), indicating pre-existence. The author dismisses metaphorical interpretations as departure from the apparent meaning without proof. He then presents the first objection from the deniers: that creating them before the Day of Judgment is futile (ʿabath). The author simply states that the weakness of this objection is apparent, implying the refutation is obvious.

Key Terms
الجنة
النار
مخلوقتان
العبث
المجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe Paradise and Hell will only be created on Judgment Day.
Correction: The author argues they already exist based on scripture, specifically the story of Adam and Eve and Quranic verses using past tense.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main evidence for the claim that Paradise and Hell are created now?
A) Rational arguments about divine wisdom.
B) The story of Adam and Eve and Quranic verses using the past tense 'prepared'.
C) Consensus of all scholars.
D) Logical deduction that they must exist for souls after death.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position that Paradise and Hell are currently created is based on explicit Quranic texts and the story of Adam, dismissing metaphorical interpretations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that Paradise and Hell are already created and exist now. How does that truth affect your sense of urgency in seeking Paradise and avoiding Hell today, not just in the distant future? What specific action can you take this week to align your life with that reality?
?
The author dismisses the objection that creating Paradise and Hell before Judgment Day is futile as obviously weak. Reflect on your own thoughts: Do you ever question Allah’s wisdom in creating things that seem ‘unnecessary’ or ‘premature’? What does this lesson teach you about trusting Allah’s plans even when you don’t see the immediate purpose?
?
The lesson states that interpreting the Quranic verses about Paradise and Hell metaphorically is a departure from the apparent meaning without evidence. Is there any area of your faith where you are tempted to explain away clear texts to suit your own comfort or desires? How can you embrace the literal meanings even when they challenge you?

Answering the Objection from Perishing
Sanusi refutes the claim that the verse of perishing contradicts their eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the three responses to the objection about perishing preserve the eternity of Paradise and Hell.

Core Idea
The verse of perishing does not disprove the eternity of Paradise and Hell.

The second objection against the pre-creation of Paradise and Hell argues that if they were created, they would be subject to the general perishing mentioned in the Quran. This passage presents the answer, offering three hermeneutical strategies to reconcile the verse with their eternity. We will explore each response and how they maintain consistency with revelation and reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Note the objection’s structure and the three-part response.
The objection uses Surah Al-Qasas 28:88 as proof.
2
Examine the three responses
Analyze each of the three responses: exclusion from generality, reinterpretation of 'perishing', and momentary annihilation. Understand how each defuses the objection.
These are hermeneutical moves, not arbitrary claims.
3
Reflect on the principles
Consider the broader principle: general texts can have exceptions, and words can carry multiple meanings. This is a standard tool in kalam.
This shows the importance of usul al-fiqh in theological argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - لو خلقتا لهلكتا، لقوله تعالى : كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه (١) وهو باطل بالنص والإجماع . قلنا : يخصان من عموم الآية، أو يحمل الهلاك على غير الفناء، أو تفنيان لحظة، وهو لا ينافي الدوام عرفاً.
Second: If they were created, they would perish, according to His statement, 'Everything is perishing except His Face’ (1), and this is false by text and consensus. We say: They are excluded from the generality of the verse, or 'perishing' is interpreted as other than annihilation, or they perish for a moment, and this does not contradict perpetuity conventionally.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection of the deniers against the pre-creation of Paradise and Hell, and the answer. The objection argues that if Paradise and Hell were created now, they would be subject to the general perishing mentioned in the Quranic verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face.' The deniers claim that this consequence is false because the texts indicate the eternity of Paradise and Hell. The answer offers three responses: (1) The verse is general but Paradise and Hell are specifically excluded by other texts; (2) The word 'perishing' (halaak) here does not mean total annihilation but rather passing away or change; (3) They might perish for a single moment but that does not contradict their ongoing existence as commonly understood.

Key Terms
هلاك
فناء
دوام
عموم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Everything is perishing' applies absolutely to all created beings, including Paradise and Hell, without exception.
Correction: The verse's generality does not preclude specific exceptions. Other texts establish the eternity of Paradise and Hell, so they are excluded from the verse's scope.

Checkpoint
How does the answer refute the second objection that Paradise and Hell would perish?
A) By denying the verse's authenticity
B) By arguing the verse only applies to mundane objects
C) By giving three hermeneutical possibilities: exclusion, reinterpretation of 'perishing', or momentary annihilation
D) By claiming Paradise and Hell are not created

Key Takeaway
The eternity of Paradise and Hell is not undermined by the general verse 'Everything is perishing' because it admits exceptions, reinterpretation, or momentary perishing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Reflect on a time when you encountered a Quranic verse that seemed to contradict something you firmly believed. Did you, like the objectors in this lesson, jump to a conclusion, or did you seek a deeper understanding? What would it look like for you to follow Sanusi's method of considering multiple valid interpretations before dismissing a truth?
?
The objection assumed a simplistic reading of 'everything is perishing.' Where in your own life do you settle for simplistic readings of scripture that lead you to doubt or reject what Allah has made clear? How can you cultivate a habit of deeper study and trust in the scholars who reconcile seemingly conflicting texts?
?
Sanusi offers three possible reconciliations. Which of these approaches—specification, semantic reinterpretation, or concession of momentary perishing—resonates most with your own struggle to hold onto faith when faced with intellectual doubts? What step will you take this week to apply that same approach to a doubt you currently face?

Answering the Objection on the Location of Paradise and Hell
Refutes the claim that Paradise and Hell cannot exist spatially now.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Maqasid refutes the philosophical objection that Paradise and Hell cannot currently exist in a spatial realm.

Core Idea
Philosophical objections to theology are not binding unless their premises are necessary.

In this passage, the author confronts a sophisticated objection against the existence of Paradise and Hell now. The objection tries to prove impossibility by examining possible locations. The author's response demonstrates that the objection rests on philosophical assumptions that are not universally accepted, and offers alternative spatial models consistent with divine power.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and its structure
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the objection is presented as a conditional: if Paradise and Hell exist now, they must be either in this world or another. Each option is argued to be impossible.
2
Analyze the two branches
The objection first rules out being in this world: not in spheres or elements due to size and reincarnation. Then rules out another world: it would create a void and conflicting natural places.
The argument about two natural places for a single element is a key physical objection.
3
Understand the author's answer
The author dismisses most premises as philosophical, not necessary. He suggests that both worlds could be within a greater sphere, and elements can have different natures in each world. He also clarifies the definition of reincarnation to avoid confusion.
Notice the author does not accept the premise that a second world would necessarily be spherical with a void.
4
Reflect on the broader principle
Consider how this objection and answer illustrate the relationship between reason and revelation in Islamic theology: rational arguments are valid only if their premises are self-evident or derived from revelation.
This lesson shows the importance of knowing what counts as a binding proof in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث .. لو وجدتا فإما في هذا العالم، ولا يتصور في أفلاكه لامتناع الخرق والصعود والهبوط، ولا في عناصره، لأنها لا تسع جنة عرضها كعرض السماء ، ولأن عود الروح إلى البدن في عالم العناصر تناسخ . وإما في عالم آخر، وهو باطل لأنه لافتقاره إلى تحدد الجهات يكون كرياً ، فيكون بين العالمين خلاء، ولأنه يشتمل على عناصر وأحياز طبيعية لها، فيكون لعنصر واحد حيزان ،طبیعیان ویلزم میله إليه وعنه . قلنا : أكثر المقدمات فلسفية، مع أنه لا يمتنع كون العالمين في محيط بهما بمنزلة تدويرين في فلك، ولا كون العناصر مختلفة الطبائع، ولا كون تحيزها في أحد العالمين حيز طبيعي . والتناسخ تعلق النفس في هذا العالم ببدن آخر .
Third: If they existed now, then either in this world—and they cannot be conceived in its spheres due to the impossibility of piercing, ascending, and descending, nor in its elements because they cannot contain a Garden whose width is as the width of the sky, and because the return of the soul to the body in the elemental world is reincarnation—or in another world, and this is false because, due to its need to be determined by directions, it would be spherical, so there would be a void between the two worlds, and because it contains elements and natural places for them, so one element would have two natural places, necessitating its inclination toward and away from them. We say: Most of these premises are philosophical, although it is not impossible that the two worlds be in an encompassing sphere like two circles within a sphere, nor that the elements have different natures, nor that their being located in one of the two worlds be a natural place. And reincarnation is the attachment of the soul in this world to another body.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection of the deniers and the answer. The objection argues that if Paradise and Hell are currently existing, they must be either within this world or in another world. Within this world, they cannot be in the celestial spheres because moving through them is impossible, nor in the elemental region because they cannot contain the vast Garden described, and because the return of souls to bodies in this elemental world would imply reincarnation (tanasukh), which is false. If in another world, that world would need to be determined by directions, making it spherical and leaving a void between the two worlds; moreover, elements would have two natural places, causing contradiction. The answer states that most of these premises are philosophical and not binding. It asserts that it is not impossible for both worlds to be encompassed within a greater sphere, like two orbits within a single sphere, nor for elements to have different natures, nor for their place in one world to be their natural place. Reincarnation is defined not as the soul moving to another body in this world, but as attachment to a different body in this world—which is not relevant here.

Key Terms
عالم
خلاء
تناسخ
حيز طبيعي
فلسفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The return of souls to bodies in the hereafter is a form of reincarnation (tanasukh), which is false.
Correction: Reincarnation specifically means the soul attaching to another body in this world; the resurrection of bodies in the hereafter is a different concept.

Checkpoint
What is the main flaw the author identifies in the third objection regarding location?
A) The objection assumes Paradise and Hell are within this universe
B) The objection relies on philosophical premises that are not necessarily accepted
C) The objection forgets that Paradise and Hell are spiritual, not physical
D) The objection is based on a misreading of the Quran

Key Takeaway
The objection fails because it relies on philosophical premises that are not necessary, and alternative spatial arrangements are possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that philosophical objections to theological truths can be dismissed if their premises are not necessary. Think of a time you rejected or doubted an Islamic teaching because of a 'scientific' or 'rational' objection that you assumed was absolute. What was that objection, and what premise did you assume? Are you willing to revisit that assumption today, even if it is uncomfortable?
?
The objectors in this lesson argued that Paradise and Hell cannot exist now because they couldn't conceive of a spatial arrangement. Do you ever find yourself limiting God's power based on your own inability to imagine how something could be? What specific aspect of the unseen do you struggle to accept because you cannot visualize it? How will you train yourself to submit to revelation instead of your imagination?
?
The refutation shows that theological truths do not depend on accepting Greek philosophical premises. Now examine your own understanding of Islam: Are there any beliefs you hold that are actually based on cultural or philosophical assumptions rather than the primary sources? What would it cost you to strip those away and adhere strictly to what the Qur'an and Sunnah affirm?

First Proof: The Story of Adam and Consensus
Sanusi presents the Sunni consensus and the first proof from the story of Adam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the story of Adam and Eve and the consensus of Muslims provide evidence that Paradise and Hell are already created.

Core Idea
The Garden of Adam is not an earthly garden; it is the eternal Paradise.

This lesson examines the first of two proofs for the pre-creation of Paradise and Hell. The author draws on the Quranic narrative of Adam and Eve and the consensus of early Muslims to argue that Paradise and Hell exist now. We will see why interpreting Adam's Garden as a literal earthly garden is rejected as contradictory to religion and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice how the author states the position of the majority and then presents the first proof.
2
Identify the two components of the proof
The proof has two parts: (1) the story of Adam and Eve in the Garden, and (2) the consensus of Muslims before the emergence of opponents. Identify each part.
The consensus strengthens the scriptural evidence.
3

The author argues that interpreting Adam's Garden as an earthly garden would be 'tampering with religion' and 'contradicting the consensus of Muslims.' Think about why that is a strong argument.
If early Muslims all agreed on a certain interpretation, later reinterpretation is difficult to justify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جمهور المسلمين على أن الجنة والنار مخلوقتان الآن، خلافاً لأبي هاشم والقاضي عبد الجبار (٣) ، ومن يجري مجراهما من المعتزلة ، حيث زعموا أنهما إنما يخلقان يوم الجزاء لنا وجهان الأول - قصة آدم وحواء ، وإسكانهما الجنة ، ثم إخراجهما عنها بأكل الشجرة، وكونهما يخصفان عليهما من ورق الجنة على ما نطق به الكتاب والسنة، وانعقد عليه الإجماع قبل ظهور المخالفين، وحملهما على بستان من بساتين الدنيا يجري مجرى التلاعب بالدين والمراغمة لإجماع المسلمين، ثم لا قائل بخلق الجنة دون النار، فثبوتها ثبوتها .
The majority of Muslims hold that Paradise and Hell are created now, contrary to Abu Hashim, Qadi Abd al-Jabbar (3), and those who follow them among the Mu‘tazila, as they claimed that they are only created on the Day of Recompense. We have two proofs. To interpret this as a garden of earthly gardens would amount to tampering with religion and contradicting the consensus of Muslims. Moreover, no one claims creation of Paradise without Hell, so the proof for one is proof for the other.

Commentary
This passage states the Sunni position that Paradise and Hell are already created, contrary to the Mu‘tazilite view that they will be created on the Day of Judgment. The author gives the first of two proofs: the story of Adam and Eve. The Quran and Sunnah narrate that Allah placed Adam and Eve in a garden (Jannah), they ate from the tree, and they were expelled. The author argues that this garden cannot be interpreted as an earthly garden because that would be distorting religion and rejecting the consensus of Muslims. Furthermore, no one distinguishes between Paradise and Hell in terms of creation; if one is created, the other is created. The consensus before the emergence of the Mu‘tazilites supports this understanding.

Second Proof: Explicit Quranic Verses in Past Tense
Cites verses describing Paradise and Hell in past tense as proof of creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the use of past-tense verbs in Quranic descriptions of Paradise and Hell serves as evidence for their pre-creation.

Core Idea
Past-tense Quranic descriptions of Paradise and Hell indicate their actual prior existence.

This lesson presents the second proof from the text: explicit Quranic verses that describe Paradise and Hell in the past tense. The author cites several verses and argues that interpreting them as mere rhetorical future expressions is contrary to the apparent meaning. You will learn the strength of this evidence and the rebuttal to a common alternative interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the specific verses cited: they all describe Paradise or Hell using past-tense verbs like 'prepared' and 'brought near'.
The verses are: 53:13-15, 3:133, 57:21, 26:90, 3:131, 26:91.
2
Identify the author's argument
The author lists these verses as explicit evidence (آيات صريحة) for the pre-creation of Paradise and Hell. The past-tense form indicates that these places already exist.
3
Understand the rebuttal to counter-interpretation
Some may argue that past tense here is rhetorical (مبالغة) to emphasize future certainty, like in 'the Trumpet is blown' (36:51). The author rejects this: such a shift from apparent meaning requires contextual evidence (قرينة), which is absent here.
The default is to take past tense literally unless there is compelling reason otherwise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - الآيات الصريحة في ذلك كقوله تعالى : ( ولقد رآه نزلة أخرى ، عند سدرة المنتهى عندها جنة المأوى (١) وكقوله في حق الجنة: أعدت للمتقين ) (٢) و أعدت للذين آمنوا بالله ورسوله ) (٣) وأزلفت الجنة للمتقين () وفي حق النار :: أعدت للكافرين ()، وبرزت الجحيم للغاوين ) وحملها على التعبير عن المستقبل بلفظ الماضي مبالغة في تحققه مثل : ونفخ في الصور (۷) ونادى أصحاب الجنة أصحاب النار (۸) خلاف الظاهر، فلا يعدل إليه بدون قرينة .
Second: The explicit verses about that, such as His statement, 'And he certainly saw him in another descent, at the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary — near it is the Garden of Refuge’ (1), and His statement regarding Paradise: 'Prepared for the righteous’ (2), and 'Prepared for those who believe in Allah and His Messenger’ (3), and 'And Paradise is brought near for the righteous’ ( ), and regarding Hell: 'Prepared for the disbelievers’ ( ), and 'And the Blazing Fire is exposed for the deviators’ ( ). To interpret these as expressing the future by using the past tense as exaggeration of its certainty, like 'And the Trumpet is blown’ (7) and 'And the companions of Paradise call to the companions of the Fire’ (8), is contrary to the apparent meaning, so one should not adopt it without evidence.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage gives the second proof for the pre-creation of Paradise and Hell: explicit Quranic verses that describe them using past-tense verbs (e.g., 'prepared,' 'brought near,' 'exposed'). The author acknowledges that some might interpret these past-tense forms as referring to future events for rhetorical emphasis (like the verse 'and the Trumpet is blown' which is future but expressed in past tense). However, he argues that such an interpretation is contrary to the apparent (zahir) meaning and cannot be adopted without contextual evidence. The default is to take the past tense as indicating actual past or present existence.

Key Terms
آيات صريحة
إعداد
مبالغة
ظاهر
صيغة الماضي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Quranic past-tense verbs about the afterlife are merely rhetorical future expressions.
Correction: While some verses use past tense for future events, the default interpretation of past tense is actual past existence. Verses about Paradise and Hell being 'prepared' should be taken literally unless there is clear contextual evidence to interpret them as future emphasis.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Explicit Quranic verses describing Paradise and Hell in the past tense provide strong evidence for their pre-creation, as the apparent meaning indicates prior existence and alternative rhetorical interpretations lack evidence.

Three Objections and Their Refutations
Lists and answers the three objections against pre-creation of Paradise and Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three objections raised by deniers against the pre-creation of Paradise and Hell and the theological responses that refute them.

Core Idea
God's actions are never futile; objections based on pre-creation collapse under scrutiny.

This passage summarizes the deniers' three main arguments against the creation of Paradise and Hell before the Day of Judgment, along with the rebuttals. The first objection is dismissed as weak, the second is answered with scriptural and logical reasoning, and the third is refuted by earlier arguments. Here we see the final recapitulation of the debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three objections
Read the passage and list the three objections: futility, perishing verse, and location dilemma.
The deniers' arguments are numbered in the text.
2
Study the refutation of each
Notice how the first is dismissed as obviously weak, the second uses specification and reinterpretation, and the third is stated to be false without new answer here.
The second refutation is the most detailed.
3
Understand the nuance of eternal existence
Consider the explanation that eternity does not mean absolute non-cessation but allows for renewal, like food.
This clarifies a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمسك المنكرون بوجوه : الأول - أن خلقهما قبل يوم الجزاء عبث لا يليق بالحكيم. وضعفه ظاهر . الثاني - أنهما لو خلقتا لهلكنا لقوله تعالى: كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه (۹) واللازم باطل للإجماع على دوامهما ، وللنصوص الشاهدة بدوام أكل الجنة وظلها . وأجيب بتخصيصها من آية الهلاك جمعاً بين الأدلة، وبحمل الهلاك على غير الفناء كما مر، وبأن الدوام المجمع عليه هو أنه لا انقطاع لبقائهما، ولا انتهاء لوجودهما بحيث لا يبقيان على العدم زماناً يعتد به، كما في دوام المأكول، فإنه على التجدد والانقضاء قطعاً (۱۰) ، وهذا لا ينافي فناء لحظة . الثالث - أنهما لو وجدتا الآن فإما في هذا العالم، أو في عالم آخر، وكلاهما باطل .
The deniers clung to points: First: That creating them before the Day of Recompense is futile, unbefitting the Wise. Its weakness is apparent. Second: That if they were created, we would perish, according to His statement, 'Everything is perishing except His Face’ (9), and the consequence is false because of consensus on their eternity and the texts witnessing the eternity of eating and shade of Paradise. It was answered by specifying them from the verse of perishing to reconcile the evidences, and by interpreting 'perishing' as other than annihilation, as previously mentioned, and by the fact that the agreed-upon eternity is that there is no interruption of their existence and no end to their existence such that they would not remain over a significant period of non-existence, like the continuity of eaten food, for it is certainly in a state of renewal and passing away, and this does not conflict with perishing for a moment. Third: That if they existed now, then either in this world or in another world, and both are false.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage summarizes the three main objections of the deniers against the pre-creation of Paradise and Hell, along with the answers. The first objection is that creating them before the Day of Judgment is futile (عبث) and unbefitting God's wisdom; the author dismisses it as obviously weak. The second objection uses the 'perishing' verse again; the answer repeats the earlier points: specification of the verse, reinterpreting 'perishing', and the nuanced understanding of eternal existence as not requiring absolute non-cessation but allowing momentary change. The third objection about location is stated but not given a new answer here; the answer was already detailed earlier. This serves as a concise recapitulation of the debate.

Misconception: Thinking that 'futility' (عبث) is a valid argument against God's actions without considering purpose in the afterlife.
Correction: The passage shows that the objection is weak, as God's wisdom encompasses purposes beyond immediate human understanding.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The deniers' three objections are refuted through careful scriptural interpretation and logical reasoning, affirming that pre-creation is neither futile nor contradictory.

Second Proof: Explicit Quranic Verses
Argument from explicit Quranic verses for pre-creation of Paradise and Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how explicit Quranic verses in the past tense serve as evidence for the pre-creation of Paradise and Hell, and why interpreting them as future references is not the apparent meaning.

Core Idea
Quranic past tense verses like 'prepared' indicate Paradise and Hell already exist.

This passage presents the second proof: explicit Quranic verses that use the past tense to describe Paradise and Hell. The author lists several verses and then addresses a potential counterargument. You will see how the apparent meaning supports pre-creation.

The Second Objection: Perishing of All Things
Second objection from Quranic perishing verse and three-part answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection against the createdness of Paradise and Hell, and the three-part answer that reconciles the verse 'Everything is perishing' with their permanence.

Core Idea
The verse 'Everything is perishing' does not necessitate annihilation of Paradise; it can be excepted or reinterpreted.

The second objection attempts to prove that Paradise and Hell must perish because the Quran says everything perishes except Allah. In response, scholars offer three nuanced arguments that harmonize the verse with the established permanence of Paradise and Hell. This lesson unpacks each part of the answer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and its Quranic basis
Read the first sentence of the passage to see the objection: if Paradise and Hell were created, they would perish, citing 'Everything is perishing except His Face.'
The objection relies on a general Quranic statement.
2
Understand why the consequence is rejected
The author says the consequence is false because of consensus and texts affirming permanence. Note the terms: 'دوام' (permanence) and 'هلاك' (perishing).
This shows the objection conflicts with established beliefs.
3
Examine the first answer: exception (تخصيص)
The first answer is that Paradise and Hell are excepted from the general rule of the verse, reconciling all evidences. This is a common method in usul al-fiqh.
Scholars use تخصيص to harmonize seemingly conflicting texts.
4
Examine the second answer: reinterpretation of 'perishing'
The second answer interprets 'هلاك' as something other than complete annihilation (فناء). This avoids the problematic implication.
This approach distinguishes between two types of perishing.
5
Examine the third answer: definition of permanence
The third answer defines 'دوام' as not ceasing for any considerable time, like food that is constantly renewed. A momentary annihilation does not contradict this.
This clarifies what permanence means in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - أنهما لو خلقتا لهلكنا لقوله تعالى: كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه واللازم باطل للإجماع على دوامهما ، وللنصوص الشاهدة بدوام أكل الجنة وظلها . وأجيب بتخصيصها من آية الهلاك جمعاً بين الأدلة، وبحمل الهلاك على غير الفناء كما،مر، وبأن الدوام المجمع عليه هو أنه لا انقطاع لبقائهما، ولا انتهاء لوجودها بحيث لا يبقيان على العدم زماناً يعتد به، كما في دوام المأكول، فإنه على التجدد والانقضاء قطعاً، وهذا لا ينافي فناء لحظة .
The second: That if they were created they would have perished due to His saying, the Most High: 'Everything is perishing except His Face.' And the necessary consequence is false by consensus on their permanence, and by texts attesting to the permanence of the eating of Paradise and its shade. And it was answered by making them an exception from the verse of perishing to reconcile the evidences, and by interpreting perishing as other than annihilation, as has passed, and that the agreed-upon permanence is that there is no interruption of their continuance, nor end of their existence such that they remain in non-existence for any considerable time, like the permanence of food, for it is subject to renewal and passing away definitely, and this does not contradict annihilation for a moment.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection: if Paradise and Hell were created, they would have perished because the Quran says 'Everything is perishing except His Face.' The author rejects the consequence as false because there is consensus on their permanence and Quranic proofs affirm the everlasting eating and shade. The answer has three parts: (1) Paradise and Hell are excepted (تخصيص) from the general rule of the verse to harmonize all evidences; (2) 'perishing' (هلاك) in that verse means something other than complete annihilation (فناء), as previously explained; (3) the agreed-upon permanence means they never cease to exist for any significant period—like food which is constantly renewed and consumed, but still persists in a sense. A momentary annihilation does not contradict their permanent state.

Key Terms
هلاك
فناء
دوام
تخصيص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic verse 'Everything is perishing' necessarily means Paradise and Hell will perish.
Correction: Scholars reconcile the verse by making them an exception or interpreting 'perishing' as not meaning complete annihilation, preserving their permanence.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT part of the answer to the second objection?
A) Paradise and Hell are excepted from the perishing verse.
B) The word 'perishing' means complete annihilation.
C) The permanence of Paradise means no significant period of non-existence.
D) The example of food shows renewal and passing away.

Key Takeaway
The second objection is answered by either excepting Paradise and Hell from the perishing verse, reinterpreting 'perishing,' or clarifying that their permanence allows for momentary change without cessation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Paradise and Hell are permanent as this lesson argues, and you will face eternal reward or punishment, then what action have you deliberately put off today that you know is required for the Hereafter? Will you do it within the next 24 hours?
?
The lesson shows that permanence can coexist with change and renewal. When you think of your own soul, which is also permanent, what small but recurring sin do you allow to 'renew' itself daily, assuming God overlooks it? How will you cut its renewal today?
?
The objector argued that creation implies perishing, but the scholars answered by reconciling texts with reasoning. In your life, where do you use an isolated verse or hadith to avoid accountability for the Hereafter, ignoring the broader picture of God's mercy and justice? What would change if you reconciled all evidence honestly?

The True Location of Paradise and Hell
The author states the majority view and then advocates deferring knowledge of the location of Paradise and Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct theological stance regarding the location of Paradise and Hell, and why deferring knowledge to Allah is more appropriate.

Core Idea
The location of Paradise and Hell is known only to Allah — we should not speculate.

This concluding passage from the author addresses a common question: where are Paradise and Hell located? While many scholars have offered opinions based on scriptural hints, the author argues that no explicit text settles the matter. Therefore, the safest and most correct position is to entrust this knowledge to Allah alone.

Guided Path

This reflects a cautious theological approach.

The Punishment of the Grave is True
The author affirms the punishment of the grave with three Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the punishment of the grave is a literal reality affirmed by scriptural evidence.

Core Idea
The grave holds real punishment for the wicked, proven by scripture.

In this passage, the author affirms a core Sunni doctrine: the reality of questioning and punishment in the grave. He provides three Quranic verses as evidence without further elaboration. This lesson unpacks the scriptural basis for this belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic once to get the rhythm, then the translation to understand the meaning.
The Arabic is short; read it aloud if possible.
2
Identify the three verses cited
Notice which surahs and contexts these verses come from. How do they support the punishment of the grave?
These verses are often interpreted as referring to the barzakh (intermediate state).
3
Understand the doctrine
Reflect on the logical connection between the verses and the doctrine. Why is this important in Sunni theology?
The doctrine differentiates Sunni orthodoxy from metaphorical interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث السادس - سؤال القبر وعذابه حق لقوله تعالى النار يعرضون عليها غدواً وعشياً) ( أغرقوا فأدخلوا ناراً ) (ربنا أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين)
The sixth topic: The questioning of the grave and its punishment are true because of His statement: 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening' and 'They were drowned and then entered a Fire' and 'Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and You have given us life twice.'
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This brief passage affirms a key doctrine of Sunni Islam: the reality of the interrogation and punishment in the grave. The author cites three Quranic verses as evidence. The first verse from Surah Ghafir (40:46) indicates that the people of Pharaoh are exposed to the Fire morning and evening, which is interpreted as happening in the barzakh (intermediate state). The second verse from Surah Nuh (71:25) states that the disbelievers were drowned and then entered a Fire, which again is understood to occur after death but before the Day of Judgment. The third verse from Surah Ghafir (40:11) mentions being caused to die twice and given life twice, which is often interpreted as a reference to death in this world, then a life in the grave, then death again, and finally resurrection. These verses are used by Sunni theologians to prove that the punishment of the grave is a reality that will be experienced by the wicked.

C) ربنا أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين
D) إن الذين كفروا لهم عذاب شديد

Key Takeaway
The punishment of the grave is a literal doctrine proven by Quranic verses referring to punishment in the intermediate state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Do you treat the punishment of the grave as a literal reality or just a comforting metaphor? If it is literal, how would your priorities shift? Commit to memorizing one of these three verses this week as a constant reminder that your deeds follow you into the grave.

The Location of Paradise and Hell: Tawaqquf
Conclusion on the location of Paradise and Hell with tawaqquf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari position on the location of Paradise and Hell is to refrain from definitive assertion and delegate knowledge to Allah.

Core Idea
The location of Paradise and Hell is known only to Allah.

In this conclusion, the author addresses a question that many Muslims have wondered about: where exactly are Paradise and Hell? Although some scholars have suggested locations based on scriptural hints, the author insists that no definitive evidence exists. He presents the majority view but then establishes the correct methodology: tawaqquf (refraining) and tafwīḍ (delegating knowledge to Allah). This reflects a core principle of the Ash'ari tradition: not to go beyond what the Qur'an and Sunnah explicitly state.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author repeats the majority view in a slightly different wording.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage presents both the majority opinion (Paradise above, Hell below) and the author's conclusion (tawaqquf). Find each and note the evidence cited for the majority view.
3
Reflect on why tawaqquf is the truth
Ask yourself why the author insists on refraining despite the majority view. Consider the explicit statement that no clear text has come. This connects to the principle of not speculating in matters of the unseen.
The author uses the word 'al-ḥaqq' twice to emphasize the correct position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة - لا قطع بمكان الجنة والنار. والأكثرون على أن الجنة فوق السماوات السبع وتحت العرش، لقوله تعالى: {عند سدرة المنتهى عندها جنة المأوى} وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «سقف الجنة عرش الرحمن» والنار تحت الأرضين. والحق التوقف. لم يرد نص صريح في تعيين مكان الجنة والنار. والأكثرون على أن الجنة فوق السموات السبع وتحت العرش تشبثاً بقوله تعالى: {عند سدرة المنتهى عندها جنة المأوى} وقوله عليه السلام: «سقف الجنة عرش الرحمن والنار تحت الأرضين السبع». والحق تفويض ذلك إلى علم العليم الخبير.

The majority are of the opinion that Paradise is above the seven heavens and beneath the Throne, due to His statement: {At the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary, near it is the Garden of Refuge} (53:14-15) and his statement, peace be upon him: 'The ceiling of Paradise is the Throne of the Merciful' and Hell is under the earths. And the truth is to refrain. No explicit text has come specifying the location of Paradise and Hell. This passage is a conclusion (khātima) on the location of Paradise and Hell. The author first states that there is no definitive textual evidence specifying their location. For Hell, they say it is under the earths. However, the author declares that the correct position is tawaqquf (refraining from assertion) and tafwīḍ (delegating knowledge to Allah). This reflects the Ash'ari principle of not speculating on matters not clearly revealed.

Key Takeaway
The correct Ash'ari position on the location of Paradise and Hell is to refrain from making any definitive claim and to delegate knowledge of it to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Evidences for Grave Questioning and Torment
Author cites Quranic verses and hadith as evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural and hadith evidence that establishes the reality of the grave's questioning and torment.

Core Idea
The Quran and mutawatir hadiths affirm life and accountability in the grave.

The author opens this chapter by directly affirming the reality of the grave's questioning and torment, then immediately supports the claim with multiple Quranic verses and a well-known hadith. This lesson presents these foundational proofs, which form the bedrock of the subsequent discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic evidence carefully
Read the passage containing the Quranic verses and the hadith. Notice how each verse is cited as proof for a different aspect of grave life.
Pay attention to the phrase 'the second is only in the grave' which interprets a key verse.
2
Identify the key verses and their implications
The verses about Pharaoh's people, the drowning of Noah's people, the two deaths and two lives, and the provision of sustenance all point to an intermediate life in the grave.
3
Understand the significance of mutawatir hadith
The author states that the hadiths on this topic are mutawatir in meaning, meaning they convey certain knowledge due to their widespread transmission.
Mutawatir is a technical term for widespread, uninterrupted transmission.
4
Reflect on the importance of this doctrine
This lesson establishes that belief in grave questioning and torment is a core Sunnī creedal matter based on both Quran and Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث السادس - سؤال القبر وعذابه حق لقوله تعالى: {النار يعرضون عليها غدواً وعشياً} {أغرقوا فأدخلوا ناراً} {ربنا أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين} وليست الثانية إلا في القبر. {يرزقون فرحين بما آتاهم الله} ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «القبر روضة من رياض الجنة، أو حفرة من حفر النيران». والأحاديث في هذا الباب متواترة المعنى. تمسك المنكرون بالسمع والعقل. أما السمع فقوله تعالى: {لا يذوقون فيها الموت إلا الموتة الأولى} ولو كان في القبر حياة - ولا محالة - يعقبها موت لكان قبل الجنة موتتان. وقوله: {وكنتم أمواتاً فأحياكم ثم يميتكم ثم يحييكم}. وقوله تعالى حكاية: {ربنا أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين} ولو كان في القبر إحياء لكانت الإحياءات ثلاثة في الدنيا، وفي القبر، وفي الحشر. والجواب - أن إثبات الواحد أو الاثنين لا ينافي الثاني والثالث. ثم الظاهر أن قوله تعالى: {ثم يحييكم} الإحياء في الآخرة، ولم يتعرض لما في القبر، لأنه لخفاء أمره، وضعف أثره لا يصلح في معرض الترغيب في الإيمان والتعجيب من الكفر. وأن قولهم: {ربنا أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين} في الدنيا وفي القبر. وترك ما في الآخرة لأنه معاين. وقيل: بل القبر والحشر، لأن المراد إحياء يعقبه علم ضروري بالله واعتراف بالذنوب. وأما العقل فلأن اللذة والألم والمكالمة، ونحو ذلك تتوقف على الحياة المتوقفة.
The sixth chapter - The questioning of the grave and its torment are true, due to His statement: {The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening} (40:46), {They were drowned and then made to enter a Fire} (71:25), {Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and given us life twice} (40:11) - and the second is only in the grave. {They are provided sustenance, rejoicing in what Allah has given them} (3:169-170). And due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'The grave is a garden from the gardens of Paradise, or a pit from the pits of Hellfire.' And the hadiths on this topic are mutawatir in meaning. The deniers clung to scriptural and rational arguments. As for the scriptural, His statement: {They will not taste death therein except the first death} (44:56) - if there were life in the grave, inevitably followed by death, there would be two deaths before Paradise. And His statement: {And you were dead, then He gave you life, then He will cause you to die, then He will give you life} (2:28). And His statement, in narration: {Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and given us life twice} (40:11) - if there were life in the grave, the lives would be three: in the world, in the grave, and in the resurrection. And the answer: that affirming one or two does not negate the second or third. Moreover, it is apparent that His statement: {then He will give you life} refers to life in the Hereafter, and it did not address what is in the grave because of the hiddenness of its matter and the weakness of its effect, not suitable in the context of encouraging belief and expressing wonder at disbelief. And that their saying: {Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and given us life twice} is in the world and in the grave. And He omitted what is in the Hereafter because it is witnessed. And it is said: rather the grave and the resurrection, because what is meant is a life followed by necessary knowledge of Allah and confession of sins. As for the rational argument: that pleasure, pain, conversation, and the like depend on life, which is suspended.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage opens the sixth chapter affirming the reality of the grave's questioning and torment ('adhāb al-qabr). The author first presents the doctrinal claim and supports it with Quranic verses: the exposure of Pharaoh's people to the Fire morning and evening (40:46) is interpreted as happening in the grave; the drowning of Noah's people (71:25); the verse about two deaths and two lives (40:11) where the second death is in the grave; and the verse about martyrs being provided sustenance (3:169-170). He also cites the well-known hadith that the grave is either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hell, noting that hadiths on this are mutawatir in meaning. Then he presents the objections of the deniers (al-munkirūn), who use both scriptural and rational arguments. Their scriptural objections are: (1) the verse 'They will not taste death therein except the first death' (44:56), which they claim implies no death after the first, so if there were life in the grave followed by death, there would be two deaths before Paradise; (2) the verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:28) outlining two deaths and two lives, which they argue would be exceeded if there is a life in the grave; (3) the verse from Surah Ghafir (40:11) mentioning two deaths and two lives, which they say would become three if the grave's life is counted. The answer (al-jawāb) is given: affirming one or two does not negate a third or fourth; the verse 'then He will give you life' refers to the Hereafter, not the grave, because the grave's matter is hidden and its effect weak, unsuitable for encouraging faith; the verse 'Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice...' refers to life in the world and in the grave, omitting the Hereafter because it is witnessed; an alternative interpretation says it refers to the grave and the resurrection. Finally, the rational objection is introduced: pleasure and pain require life, which is not present in the grave (the answer to this objection continues on the next page and is not included in this passage).

Key Terms
سؤال القبر
عذاب القبر
متواتر المعنى
حياة البرزخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, to what does the second life in the verse 'Rabbana amatnā ithnatayn wa ahyaytanā ithnatayn' (40:11) refer?
A) Life in the Hereafter.
B) Life in the grave.
C) Life in the world.
D) Life in the Barzakh.

Key Takeaway
The grave's questioning and torment are proven by multiple Quranic verses and a mutawatir hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight and enter your grave, would it be a garden from Paradise or a pit from Hell? What one thing can you change today to make it a garden?

Refuting the Objections to Grave Life
Author presents and refutes scriptural objections, introduces rational objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural objections raised by those who deny grave life, and the author's responses to them, as well as the rational objection that is partially presented.

Core Idea
The deniers' scriptural objections are answered by proper exegesis of the Quranic verses.

After presenting the evidence, the author turns to the arguments of those who deny the reality of grave torment. They raise both scriptural and rational objections. This lesson covers their scriptural objections and the author's carefully reasoned responses. The rational objection is also introduced, though its full refutation continues beyond this section.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections and responses in order
The passage first presents the deniers' scriptural arguments, then the author's answers. Follow the logical flow carefully.
2
Analyze the first objection from Surah al-Dukhan (44:56)
The deniers claim this verse implies only one death before Paradise, contradicting a death after grave life. Note the author's response that affirming one or two does not negate a third.
3
Consider the second objection from Surah al-Baqarah (2:28)
The verse outlines two deaths and two lives; the author explains that 'then He will give you life' refers to the Hereafter, not the grave.
4
Understand the alternative interpretations of 40:11
The author offers two possible interpretations of 'two lives': world and grave, or grave and resurrection. See how each avoids contradiction.
5
Note the rational objection left incomplete
The passage ends with the rational objection about life being necessary for pleasure/pain; the full answer is on the next page.
This lesson covers only what is present in this section.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث السادس - سؤال القبر وعذابه حق لقوله تعالى: {النار يعرضون عليها غدواً وعشياً} {أغرقوا فأدخلوا ناراً} {ربنا أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين} وليست الثانية إلا في القبر. {يرزقون فرحين بما آتاهم الله} ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «القبر روضة من رياض الجنة، أو حفرة من حفر النيران». والأحاديث في هذا الباب متواترة المعنى. تمسك المنكرون بالسمع والعقل. أما السمع فقوله تعالى: {لا يذوقون فيها الموت إلا الموتة الأولى} ولو كان في القبر حياة - ولا محالة - يعقبها موت لكان قبل الجنة موتتان. وقوله: {وكنتم أمواتاً فأحياكم ثم يميتكم ثم يحييكم}. وقوله تعالى حكاية: {ربنا أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين} ولو كان في القبر إحياء لكانت الإحياءات ثلاثة في الدنيا، وفي القبر، وفي الحشر. والجواب - أن إثبات الواحد أو الاثنين لا ينافي الثاني والثالث. ثم الظاهر أن قوله تعالى: {ثم يحييكم} الإحياء في الآخرة، ولم يتعرض لما في القبر، لأنه لخفاء أمره، وضعف أثره لا يصلح في معرض الترغيب في الإيمان والتعجيب من الكفر. وأن قولهم: {ربنا أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين} في الدنيا وفي القبر. وترك ما في الآخرة لأنه معاين. وقيل: بل القبر والحشر، لأن المراد إحياء يعقبه علم ضروري بالله واعتراف بالذنوب. وأما العقل فلأن اللذة والألم والمكالمة، ونحو ذلك تتوقف على الحياة المتوقفة.
The sixth chapter - The questioning of the grave and its torment are true, due to His statement: {The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening} (40:46), {They were drowned and then made to enter a Fire} (71:25), {Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and given us life twice} (40:11) - and the second is only in the grave. {They are provided sustenance, rejoicing in what Allah has given them} (3:169-170). And due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'The grave is a garden from the gardens of Paradise, or a pit from the pits of Hellfire.' And the hadiths on this topic are mutawatir in meaning. The deniers clung to scriptural and rational arguments. As for the scriptural, His statement: {They will not taste death therein except the first death} (44:56) - if there were life in the grave, inevitably followed by death, there would be two deaths before Paradise. And His statement: {And you were dead, then He gave you life, then He will cause you to die, then He will give you life} (2:28). And His statement, in narration: {Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and given us life twice} (40:11) - if there were life in the grave, the lives would be three: in the world, in the grave, and in the resurrection. And the answer: that affirming one or two does not negate the second or third. Moreover, it is apparent that His statement: {then He will give you life} refers to life in the Hereafter, and it did not address what is in the grave because of the hiddenness of its matter and the weakness of its effect, not suitable in the context of encouraging belief and expressing wonder at disbelief. And that their saying: {Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and given us life twice} is in the world and in the grave. And He omitted what is in the Hereafter because it is witnessed. And it is said: rather the grave and the resurrection, because what is meant is a life followed by necessary knowledge of Allah and confession of sins. As for the rational argument: that pleasure, pain, conversation, and the like depend on life, which is suspended.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage opens the sixth chapter affirming the reality of the grave's questioning and torment ('adhāb al-qabr). The author first presents the doctrinal claim and supports it with Quranic verses: the exposure of Pharaoh's people to the Fire morning and evening (40:46) is interpreted as happening in the grave; the drowning of Noah's people (71:25); the verse about two deaths and two lives (40:11) where the second death is in the grave; and the verse about martyrs being provided sustenance (3:169-170). He also cites the well-known hadith that the grave is either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hell, noting that hadiths on this are mutawatir in meaning. Then he presents the objections of the deniers (al-munkirūn), who use both scriptural and rational arguments. Their scriptural objections are: (1) the verse 'They will not taste death therein except the first death' (44:56), which they claim implies no death after the first, so if there were life in the grave followed by death, there would be two deaths before Paradise; (2) the verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:28) outlining two deaths and two lives, which they argue would be exceeded if there is a life in the grave; (3) the verse from Surah Ghafir (40:11) mentioning two deaths and two lives, which they say would become three if the grave's life is counted. The answer (al-jawāb) is given: affirming one or two does not negate a third or fourth; the verse 'then He will give you life' refers to the Hereafter, not the grave, because the grave's matter is hidden and its effect weak, unsuitable for encouraging faith; the verse 'Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice...' refers to life in the world and in the grave, omitting the Hereafter because it is witnessed; an alternative interpretation says it refers to the grave and the resurrection. Finally, the rational objection is introduced: pleasure and pain require life, which is not present in the grave (the answer to this objection continues on the next page and is not included in this passage).

Misconception: The Quranic verses about two deaths and two lives prove there is no life in the grave.
Correction: The author shows that these verses are compatible with grave life through proper interpretation: the second life in 40:11 refers to the grave, and the verses do not exclude a third phase.

Checkpoint

A) Because it is hidden and weak.
B) Because it is witnessed.
C) Because it refers to the Hereafter.
D) Because it comes after death.

Key Takeaway

The Scriptural Objection Against Life in the Grave and Its Answer
Author presents and refutes a scriptural objection to life in the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural objection to life in the grave based on Qur'anic verses and how the author refutes it by reinterpreting the verses.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's mention of two deaths does not exclude a hidden life in the grave.

In this passage, the author addresses a key scriptural objection raised by those who deny life in the grave (hayāt al-barzakh). The objectors cite several Qur'anic verses that seem to limit life to two revivals. The author provides a nuanced response, showing that these verses are not exhaustive and can be interpreted in a way that accommodates life in the grave. This lesson will walk through the objection and the author's answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the verses cited
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on the three Qur'anic verses the objectors use. Notice how they argue that there would be three revivals if life in the grave existed.
The verses are: Q. 44:56, 2:28, 40:11.
2
Understand the author's first answer
The author responds that affirming one or two deaths does not negate a third. Consider why the verses are not necessarily exhaustive.
3
Analyze the reinterpretation of the verses
The author reinterprets the verses to show that they either refer to the Hereafter or to life in the world and the grave, leaving out the Hereafter because it is evident. Identify these two interpretations.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Understand how the author's answer successfully defends life in the grave without contradicting the Qur'an.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمسك المنكرون بالسمع والعقل. أما السمع فقوله تعالى : لا يذوقون فيها الموت إلا الموتة الأولى (٣) ولو كان في القبر حياة - ولا محالة - يعقبها موت لكان قبل الجنة موتتان . وقوله : وكنتم أمواتاً فأحياكم ثم يميتكم ثم يحييكم (٤) . وقوله تعالى حكاية : ربنا أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين (٥) ولو كان في القبر إحياء لكانت الإحياءات ثلاثة في الدنيا، وفي القبر، وفي الحشر . والجواب ـ أن إثبات الواحد أو الاثنين لا ينافي الثاني والثالث . ثم الظاهر أن قوله تعالى : (ثم يحييكم) : الإحياء في الآخرة، ولم يتعرض لما في القبر، لأنه لخفاء أمره، وضعف أثره لا يصلح في معرض الترغيب في الإيمان والتعجيب من الكفر، وأن قولهم : أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين) (1) في الدنيا وفي القبر. وترك ما في الآخرة لأنه معاين. وقيل: بل القبر والحشر، لأن المراد إحياء يعقبه علم ضروري بالله، واعتراف بالذنوب
The deniers hold fast to revelation and reason. As for revelation, His statement: 'They will not taste death therein except the first death' (Q. 44:56); and if there were life in the grave - inevitably - followed by death, there would be two deaths before Paradise. And His statement: 'And you were dead, and He brought you to life, then He will cause you to die, then He will bring you to life' (Q. 2:28). And His statement, narrating: 'Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and You have given us life twice' (Q. 40:11). And if there were revival in the grave, there would be three revivals: in the world, in the grave, and in the gathering. The answer: That affirming one or two does not negate the second and third. Then it is apparent that His statement 'then He will bring you to life' means life in the Hereafter, and it does not address what is in the grave, because due to the concealment of its matter and the weakness of its effect, it is not suitable for the context of encouraging faith and expressing wonder at disbelief. And that their statement: 'You have caused us to die twice and You have given us life twice' refers to life in the world and in the grave. And it leaves out the Hereafter because it is witnessed. And it is said: rather it is the grave and the gathering, because what is meant is a life that is followed by necessary knowledge of God and acknowledgment of sins.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes a scriptural objection against the doctrine of life in the grave (hayāt al-barzakh). The objectors argue that certain Qur'anic verses imply only two deaths and two revivals, so there cannot be a third life in the grave. The author first quotes the verses: 'They will not taste death therein except the first death' (Q. 44:56), which suggests that after entering Paradise there is only one death; if there were life in the grave followed by death, there would be two deaths before Paradise. Next, 'And you were dead, and He brought you to life, then He will cause you to die, then He will bring you to life' (Q. 2:28) mentions two deaths?—?the original non-existence and earthly death?—?and two revivals. The third verse, 'Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and You have given us life twice' (Q. 40:11), similarly mentions two deaths and two revivals. The objectors conclude that if there were revival in the grave, the total would be three revivals, contradicting these texts. The author responds by first noting that affirming one or two deaths/revivals does not negate a third; the verses are not necessarily exhaustive. Then he reinterprets the verses: 'then He will bring you to life' refers to the Hereafter, not the grave, because the grave's life is too subtle and hidden to be mentioned in that context. The verse 'You have caused us to die twice and You have given us life twice' is interpreted as referring to life in the world and in the grave, leaving out the Hereafter because it is evident. Another interpretation is that the two lives are in the grave and the gathering, following a life that brings necessary knowledge of God and acknowledgment of sins. Thus the objection is answered without denying life in the grave.

Correction: The author shows that the verses are not exhaustive and can be interpreted to include life in the grave.

Key Takeaway
