?
The Mu'tazila denied the literal Sirat because they thought crossing it would be torment. Is there any aspect of the afterlife that makes you uncomfortable, such that you downplay or explain it away? How does the author's answer challenge you to trust God's mercy and power?
?
God makes the path easy so that some believers cross like lightning. Do you live with genuine confidence that God can make the impossible easy for you on the Day of Judgment, or do you secretly rely on your own deeds? What would change in your daily life if you truly believed that?

Life in the Grave: A Special Type of Life
Al-Taftazani explains the limited life in the grave and the soul issue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the position of Ahl al-Sunna regarding life in the grave and why the return of the soul is not affirmed.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunna affirm a limited life in the grave but not full soul return.

In this concluding passage, al-Taftazani clarifies the Sunni stance on the intermediate state. While it is certain that the deceased experience pain and pleasure, the return of the soul is not taken for granted. The passage also addresses a potential objection and a hadith-based difficulty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the key terms and the flow of the argument.
The passage is compact; read carefully.
2
Identify the agreed points and hesitation
Find where al-Taftazani states the consensus of Ahl al-Haqq and where they hesitated about the soul's return.
The hesitation is explicitly mentioned after the agreement.
3
Understand the objection and resolution
Note the objection that life without the soul is impossible, and how al-Taftazani refutes it by distinguishing complete life from this limited life.
The resolution uses the example of a stroke victim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قد ثبتت بالضرورة من أن للميت في القبر نوع حياة قدر ما يتألم ويتلذذ، ولكن في إعادة الروح إليه تردد وامتناع الحياة بدون الروح ممنوع . اتفق أهل الحق على أن الله يعيد إلى الميت في القبر نوع حياة قدر ما يتالم ويتلذذ ويشهد بذلك الكتاب والأخبار والآثار، لكن توقفوا في أنه هل يعاد الروح إليه أم لا؟ وما يتوهم من امتناع الحياة بدون الروح ممنوع . وإنما ذلك في الحياة الكاملة التي يكون معها القدرة والأفعال الاختيارية. وقد اتفقوا على أن الله تعالى لم يخلق في الميت القدرة والأفعال الاختيارية . فلهذا لا يعرف حياته كمن أصابته سكتة . ويشكل هذا بجوابه لمنكر ونكير على ما ورد في الحديث .
It has been established necessarily that the deceased has in the grave a type of life to the extent that he feels pain and pleasure, but regarding the return of the soul to him there is hesitation; the impossibility of life without the soul is rejected. The people of truth agreed that Allah returns to the deceased in the grave a type of life to the extent that he feels pain and pleasure, and the Book, reports, and traditions bear witness to that. But they hesitated whether the soul is returned to him or not. And what is imagined of the impossibility of life without the soul is rejected. That is only in the complete life with which power and voluntary actions exist. And they agreed that Allah the Exalted has not created in the deceased power and voluntary actions. Therefore, his life is not known, like one who has suffered a stroke. This is problematic with its answer to Munkar and Nakir as reported in the hadith.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion (khatima) discussing the nature of life in the grave and the return of the soul. The author states that it is necessarily established that the deceased has a type of life in the grave sufficient for experiencing pain and pleasure. However, there is hesitation (taraddud) about whether the soul (ruh) is returned. The impossibility of life without the soul is rejected (mamnu‘). The consensus of Ahl al-Haqq is that Allah returns to the deceased a type of life for pain and pleasure, supported by scripture, hadith, and athar. But they stopped short of affirming the return of the soul. The objection that life without the soul is impossible is dismissed as applying only to complete life involving power (qudra) and voluntary actions, which Allah does not create in the deceased. Thus, his life is hidden like a stroke victim. The passage ends by noting a difficulty in reconciling this with the hadith about the questioning by Munkar and Nakir.

Key Terms
حياة القبر
إعادة الروح
أهل الحق
منكر ونكير
الكتاب والأخبار والآثار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think life in the grave implies full corporeal life with voluntary actions and the return of the soul.
Correction: The text clarifies it is a special life sufficient for pain and pleasure, without power or voluntary actions, and without necessarily returning the soul.

Checkpoint
What do Ahl al-Haqq agree regarding the life of the deceased in the grave?
A) They affirm complete life with all capacities
B) They affirm a type of life for pain and pleasure but not the return of the soul
C) They deny any life after death until the resurrection
D) They affirm that the soul returns to the body immediately after burial

Key Takeaway
The deceased in the grave have a special life for experiencing reward and punishment, but without full soul return or voluntary actions, consistent with the hadith about Munkar and Nakir.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to experience a foretaste of the grave's life tonight—feeling pain for every sin and pleasure for every good deed—would you live tomorrow differently? What specific action would you change right now if you knew you would feel its consequence moments after burial?
?
The deceased in the grave are described as having a life like a stroke victim—aware but powerless. Do you spend your days acting as if you will be completely unconscious after death, or do you prepare for a state where every intention and deed will be felt? What habit must you break to take this seriously?
?
The passage notes a problem reconciling the limited life in the grave with the detailed questioning by Munkar and Nakir. This tension is left unresolved. How comfortable are you living with uncertainty about the unseen? Will you act on what is established or wait for complete clarity that may never come in this world?

Affirming the Ṣirāṭ and Mīzān Against Mu'tazilite Denials
Al-Taftazani affirms the Bridge and Balance, refuting Mu'tazilite denials.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite objections to the Bridge and Balance and the orthodox response affirming their literal reality as revealed by the Truthful One.

Core Idea
Eschatological realities are possible and obligatory to believe, despite rational objections.

In this passage from the seventh investigation, al-Taftazani turns to specific eschatological matters—the Bridge (ṣirāṭ), Balance (mīzān), and others—reported in the Qur'an and Sunnah. He affirms that these are possible (mumkin) and must be believed because they come from the truthful Prophet. He then presents two Mu'tazilite objections that challenge the physical description of the Bridge and the weighing of deeds, along with their metaphorical reinterpretations, and concludes with a robust response that preserves the literal reality while explaining how God facilitates the crossing and the weighing of deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic text of the seventh investigation slowly, then the literal English translation. Note the structure: affirmation, objection, interpretation, answer.
The passage is dense; pay attention to the two distinct Mu'tazilite objections.
2
Identify the two Mu'tazilite objections
The Mu'tazilites argued first that the Bridge being finer than hair and sharper than a sword would make crossing it torment, not possible; second, that deeds are accidents (a‘rāḍ) and cannot be weighed. Find these in the text.
These objections are grounded in physical and metaphysical reasoning.
3
Understand the author's response
Al-Taftazani responds by asserting that God makes the path easy so that some cross like lightning, and explains the weighing of deeds as weighing their scrolls or transforming them into luminous/dark bodies. Grasp how this counters the objections.
The response does not abandon literalism but explains the mechanism.
4
Reflect on the obligation of belief
Revisit the opening: all these matters are possible and reported by the truthful, so belief is obligatory (wājib). Consider how this frames the entire discussion.
The obligation stems from source authority, not rational demonstration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث السابع - سائر ما ورد في الكتاب والسنة من المحاسبة وأهوالها، والصراط ، والميزان ، والحوض، وتفاصيل أحوال الجنة والنار أمور ممكنة أخبر بها الصادق، فوجب التصديق وأنكر بعض المعتزلة الصراط والميزان على ما وصفا لأن ما هو أدق من الشعر، وأحد من السيف ، والعبور عليه لو أمكن فعذاب، والأعمال أعراض لا يعقل وزنها. فالصراط طريق الجنة وطريق النار، أو الأدلة الواضحة، أو العبادات والشريعة والميزان العدل الثابت في كل شيء، أو الإدراك كالحواس للمحسوسات، والعلم للمعقولات . والجواب - أن الله يسهل الطريق حتى يمر البعض كالبرق الخاطف وهكذا . حتى يخر البعض على الوجه والأعمال توزن ،صحائفها، أو تجعل الحسنات أجساماً نورانية والسيئات ظلمانية).
The seventh investigation: All that has come in the Book and the Sunnah of the accounting and its terrors, the Bridge, the Balance, the Pool, and details of the states of Paradise and Hell are possible matters reported by the Truthful One, so belief in them is obligatory. Some Mu'tazilites denied the Bridge and the Balance as described because it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword, and crossing it if possible would be torment, and deeds are accidents whose weighing is not conceivable. So the Bridge is the path to Paradise and the path to Hell, or clear evidences, or acts of worship and the Law; and the Balance is justice established in everything, or perception like the senses for sensible things and knowledge for intelligibles. The answer: God makes the path easy so that some pass like a flash of lightning and so on, until some fall on their faces. And deeds are weighed, their scrolls, or good deeds are made luminous bodies and evil deeds dark bodies.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is the seventh investigation (al-mabḥath al-sābi‘) concerning eschatological matters reported in revelation. The author begins by affirming that all such reports—accounting, terrors, the Bridge (ṣirāṭ), the Balance (mīzān), the Pool (ḥawḍ), and details of Paradise and Hell—are possible (mumkin) and reported by the Truthful (al-ṣādiq, i.e., the Prophet), so belief (taṣdīq) is obligatory. Some Mu'tazilites denied the Bridge and Balance as described, giving two objections: first, the Bridge is finer than hair and sharper than a sword, so crossing it would be torment, not something possible; second, deeds are accidents (a‘rāḍ) and cannot be weighed. The author then mentions interpretations adopted by these Mu'tazilites: the Bridge is the clear path or the Law, and the Balance is justice or perception. The response (al-jawāb) is that God makes the path easy so that some cross like a flash of lightning, while others fall on their faces. The weighing of deeds is explained as weighing their scrolls (ṣuḥuf) or transforming good deeds into luminous bodies (ajsām nūrāniyya) and evil deeds into dark bodies (ẓulmāniyya).

Key Terms
الصراط
الميزان
المعتزلة
الأعراض
صحائف الأعمال
الحسنات والسيئات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Mu'tazilite denial is based solely on rationalism without specific arguments.
Correction: The Mu'tazilites gave two concrete objections: the physical impossibility of crossing a razor-sharp bridge and the inconceivability of weighing accidents.

Checkpoint
What is one Mu'tazilite objection to the Bridge and Balance as described in revelation?
A) The Bridge is too wide to cross
B) Deeds are accidents and cannot be weighed
C) The Balance is not mentioned in the Qur'an
D) The Pool is only for the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Revealed eschatological matters must be believed literally, and rational objections can be answered by affirming God's power and providing plausible explanations for how they occur.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted or downplayed a core Islamic belief because it seemed rationally impossible or uncomfortable to accept? The Mu'tazilites denied the Bridge and Balance because they could not conceive of how they could be real. What specific belief in your own heart needs to be affirmed anew, simply because Allah's Messenger reported it? Write down one such belief and commit to repeating 'āmannā bihi' (we believe in it) daily this week.
?
The Mu'tazilites' objections about the Ṣirāṭ being too fine and deeds being unweighable were based on their own limited reasoning. In your daily life, do you ever let your own 'rational' objections override clear revelation? Identify one area where you have re-interpreted a revealed truth to fit your comfort or logic. What would it cost you to accept it literally, and how will you train yourself to submit to revelation over reason starting today?

The Horrors of the Day of Judgment: Accounting, Standing, Scrolls, Questioning, and Witnesses
Al-Taftazani enumerates five eschatological horrors with scriptural evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the major horrors of the Day of Judgment as enumerated by Al-Taftazani, based on the Qur'an and Sunnah, and why belief in them is obligatory.

Core Idea
The Day of Judgment includes five specific horrors that are literally true and obligatory to believe.

Al-Taftazani continues his discussion of eschatological matters by listing specific events of the Day of Judgment. He emphasizes that these are possible realities affirmed by revelation and consensus, not mere symbols. This passage enumerates five distinct horrors: the accounting, the standing, the flying of scrolls, the questioning, and the testimony of body parts and guardians. Each is supported by Qur'anic verses and hadith, reinforcing the need for literal belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the introduction on the reality of these matters
Understand that Al-Taftazani asserts these are possible, from Book and Sunnah, consensus, and obligatory to believe.
2
Identify the first two horrors: accounting and standing
Locate the verses and hadith for accounting (muḥāsaba) and standing (wuqūf); note the varying durations.
3
Examine the horror of flying scrolls
Look at the verses about the book in the right hand and the spread book.
4
Study the horrors of questioning and testimony
Note the ten witnesses: tongues, hands, feet, etc., and the verse.
5
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Consider that these are to be taken literally, not symbolically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في سائر السمعيات المتعلقة بأمر المعاد، وجملة الأمر أنها أمور ممكنة نطق بها الكتاب والسنة، وانعقد عليها إجماع الأمة، فيكون القول بها حقاً، والتصديق به واجباً. فمنها المحاسبة المشار إليها بقوله تعالى : ( إن الله سريع الحساب) (١). وبقوله ( عليه السلام): «حاسبوا أنفسكم قبل أن تحاسبوا» (٢) وأهوالها هول الوقوف، قيل: ألف سنة، وقيل: خمسون ألفاً، وقيل: أقل، وقيل: أكثر، والله أعلم: قال تعالى: وقفوهم إنهم مسؤولون ) (٣) ( يوم يقوم الروح والملائكة صفاً لا يتكلمون إلا من أذن له الرحمن ) (٤) وهول تطاير الكتب. قال الله تعالى: (فأما من أوتى كتابه بيمينه، فسوف يحاسب حساباً يسيراً ) (٥) وقال: وكل إنسان الزمناه طائره في عنقه ونخرج له يوم القيامة كتاباً يلقاه منشوراً ) (٦) وهول المسألة: وقفوهم إنهم مسؤولون (٧) فوربك لنسألتهم أجمعين (٨) وهول شهادة الشهود العشرة الألسنة والأيدي والأرجل، والسمع، والأبصار ،والجلود والليل والنهار والحفظة الكرام. قال الله تعالى : يوم تشهد عليهم ألسنتهم وأيديهم وأرجلهم بما كانوا يعملون) (٩) وقال : حتى إذا
Concerning all the revealed matters related to the affair of the return (ma‘ād), and the sum of the matter is that they are possible things expressed by the Book and the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community has been concluded upon them, so stating them is true and believing in them is obligatory. Among them is the accounting (muḥāsaba) referred to by His statement the Exalted: 'Indeed Allah is swift in account' (40:13). And by his statement (peace be upon him): 'Take account of yourselves before you are taken to account.' And its terrors: the terror of standing (al-wuqūf); it is said: a thousand years, and it is said: fifty thousand, and it is said: less, and it is said: more, and Allah knows best. He said the Exalted: 'And stop them; indeed they are to be questioned' (37:24); 'The day when the Spirit and the angels stand in rows, they will not speak except one whom the Most Merciful permits' (78:38). And the terror of the flying of the scrolls (taṭāyur al-kutub). Allah the Exalted said: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand, he will be judged an easy judgment' (84:7-8). And He said: 'And every human being We have fastened his deeds to his neck, and We will bring forth for him on the Day of Resurrection a book which he will see spread open' (17:13). And the terror of the questioning (al-mas’ala): 'And stop them; indeed they are to be questioned' (37:24); 'So by your Lord, We will surely question them all' (15:92). And the terror of the testimony of the ten witnesses: tongues, hands, feet, hearing, sight, skins, night and day, and the noble guardian angels. Allah the Exalted said: 'On the Day when their tongues, their hands, and their feet will testify against them as to what they used to do' (41:20). And He said: 'Until when...'
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage continues the seventh investigation, now turning to the enumeration of eschatological horrors (ahwāl) derived from revelation. The author begins by stating that all matters of the return (ma‘ād) reported in the Book and Sunnah are possible (mumkin) and have received consensus (ijmā‘) of the Muslim community, so affirming them is true (ḥaqq) and believing in them is obligatory (wājib). He then lists several horrors: first, the accounting (muḥāsaba) supported by Qur'anic verse (Surah Ghafir 40:13) and a hadith urging self-accounting. Second, the terror of standing (al-wuqūf) with varying durations—some say one thousand years, others fifty thousand, etc. He quotes verses about being stopped and questioned (Surah al-Ṣāffāt 37:24) and the day when the Spirit and angels stand. Third, the terror of the flying of the scrolls (taṭāyur al-kutub), citing verses about receiving the book in the right hand (Surah al-Inshiqāq 84:7-8) and the book being spread open (Surah al-Isrā’ 17:13). Fourth, the terror of the questioning (al-mas’ala) with verses emphasizing universal interrogation. Fifth, the terror of the testimony of the ten witnesses: the tongue, hands, feet, hearing, sight, skins, night and day, and the noble guardian angels, citing Surah Fuṣṣilat 41:20. The passage ends mid-verse with 'until when...' (ḥattā idhā).

المحاسبة
الوقوف
تطاير الكتب
المسألة
الشهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think eschatological details are merely symbolic or metaphorical.
Correction: Al-Taftazani explicitly states these are possible real events affirmed by revelation and consensus, requiring literal belief.

Checkpoint

A) The standing (wuquf)
B) The weighing of deeds on the Balance
C) The flying of the scrolls
D) The testimony of the tongue, hands, and feet

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani affirms that the horrors of the Day of Judgment are real, possible events that every Muslim must believe based on revelation and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The terror of standing could last fifty thousand years—are you living with the urgency of someone who truly believes this could be their reality, or is it just a comforting abstraction?
?
You will be questioned about everything you did. What is one deed you are currently doing that you would be ashamed to admit when asked, and what will you do about it starting now?

The Terrors of the Day of Judgment
Enumerating seven terrors of the Day of Judgment with scriptural proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the enumerated terrors of the Day of Judgment as scripturally confirmed matters that must be believed.

Core Idea
The horrors of Judgment Day are real, supported by Quran and Hadith.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid presents a vivid catalog of the terrors of the Day of Judgment, each substantiated by explicit scriptural proofs. The author begins by asserting that these are possible events affirmed by revelation and consensus, then lists seven specific horrors that believers must affirm. Engaging with this passage builds a concrete understanding of Islamic eschatology.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the foundational principle
Read the opening sentence: these are sam‘iyyāt (transmitted matters) that are possible and obligatory to believe. This sets the framework.
2
Explore each terror
Work through the seven enumerated terrors: accounting, standing, flying books, questioning, testimony, color change, and proclamation. For each, note the scriptural evidence provided.
3
Reflect on the cumulative impact
Consider why the author lists these terrors in detail and how they reinforce the seriousness of the Hereafter. Ask yourself how this affects your own belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في سائر السمعيات المتعلقة بأمر المعاد، وجملة الأمر أنها أمور ممكنة نطق بها الكتاب والسنة، وانعقد عليها إجماع الأمة، فيكون القول بها حقاً، والتصديق به واجباً. فمنها المحاسبة المشار إليها بقوله تعالى : ( إن الله سريع الحساب) (۱). وبقوله ( عليه السلام): «حاسبوا أنفسكم قبل أن تحاسبوا» (٢) وأهوالها هول الوقوف، قيل: ألف سنة، وقيل: خمسون ألفاً، وقيل: أقل، وقيل: أكثر، والله أعلم: قال تعالى: وقفوهم إنهم مسؤولون ) (۳) ( يوم يقوم الروح والملائكة صفاً لا يتكلمون إلا من أذن له الرحمن ) (٤) وهول تطاير الكتب. قال الله تعالى: (فأما من أوتى كتابه بيمينه، فسوف يحاسب حساباً يسيراً ) (٥) وقال: وكل إنسان الزمناه طائره في عنقه ونخرج له يوم القيامة كتاباً يلقاه منشوراً ) (٦) وهول المسألة: وقفوهم إنهم مسؤولون (۷) فوربك لنسألتهم أجمعين (۸) وهول شهادة الشهود العشرة الألسنة والأيدي والأرجل، والسمع، والأبصار ،والجلود والليل والنهار والحفظة الكرام. قال الله تعالى : يوم تشهد عليهم ألسنتهم وأيديهم وأرجلهم بما كانوا يعملون) (۹) وقال : حتى إذا ما جلؤوها شهد عليهم سمعهم وأبصارهم وجلودهم بما كانوا يعملون ) (۱) وقال : ما من يوم وليلة يأتي على ابن آدم إلا قال: أنا ليل ،جديد، وأنا فيما يُعمل في شهيد (٢) . وكذا قال في اليوم، وقال الله تعالى : وجاءت كل نفس معها سائق وشهيد) (۳). وهول تغير الألوان، قال الله تعالى : ( يوم تبيض وجوه وتسود وجوه ) (٤) وقال: ﴿ وجوه يومئذ مسفرة ضاحكة مستبشرة و وجوه يومئذ عليها غبرة ترهقها قترة ﴾ (٥) . وهول المناداة بالسعادة والشقاوة. وقال عليه السلام يكون عند كل كفة الميزان ملك، فإذا ترجح كفة الخير نادى ألا إن فلاناً سعد سعادة لا شقاوة بعدها أبداً. وإذا ترجح الكفة الأخرى، نادى الملك الثاني : ألا إن فلاناً شقي شقاوة لا سعادة بعدها أبداً.
Concerning all the sam‘iyyāt (scripturally transmitted matters) related to the affair of the Final Return, and the summary is that they are possible matters spoken of by the Book and the Sunnah, and the consensus of the Ummah has been established upon them, so affirming them is truth and believing in them is obligatory. Among them is the accounting (muḥāsaba) referred to by His saying the Exalted: 'Indeed Allah is swift in account' (1) and by his saying (peace be upon him): 'Call yourselves to account before you are called to account' (2). And among its terrors is the terror of standing; it is said: a thousand years, and it is said: fifty thousand, and it is said: less, and it is said: more, and Allah knows best. He the Exalted said: 'And stop them; indeed they are to be questioned' (3) 'On the Day when the Spirit and the angels stand in rows, they do not speak except one whom the Most Merciful permits' (4). And the terror of the flying of the books. Allah the Exalted said: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand, he will be accounted with an easy account' (5) and said: 'And every human being We have fastened his omens about his neck, and We will bring forth for him on the Day of Judgment a book which he will receive spread open' (6). And the terror of the questioning: 'And stop them; indeed they are to be questioned' (7) and 'So by your Lord, We will surely question them all' (8). And the terror of the testimony of the ten witnesses: the tongues, the hands, the feet, the hearing, the sight, the skins, and the night and the day, and the noble guardians. Allah the Exalted said: 'On the Day when their tongues, their hands, and their feet will testify against them about what they used to do' (9) and said: 'Until, when they have come to it, their hearing, their sight, and their skins will testify against them about what they used to do' (1). And he said: 'There is no day and night that comes upon the son of Adam except that it says: I am a new day, and I am a witness to what is done in me' (2). And likewise he said concerning the day. And Allah the Exalted said: 'And every soul will come with a driver and a witness' (3). And the terror of the change of colors. Allah the Exalted said: 'On the Day when faces are whitened and faces are blackened' (4) and said: 'Faces on that Day will be radiant, laughing, rejoicing. And faces on that Day will have upon them dust, covered with gloom' (5). And the terror of the proclamation of happiness and misery. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'At each pan of the scale there will be an angel; when the pan of good deeds outweighs, he calls out: Verily so-and-so is happy with a happiness after which there is no misery ever. And when the other pan outweighs, the second angel calls out: Verily so-and-so is miserable with a misery after which there is no happiness ever.'
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage enumerates the various terrors (ahwāl) of the Day of Judgment that fall under the category of sam‘iyyāt (matters known by revelation). The author begins by affirming that these are possible matters confirmed by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, making belief in them obligatory. He then lists the terrors in sequence: (1) the accounting (muḥāsaba) itself, with a Quranic verse and a hadith; (2) the terror of the standing (hawl al-wuqūf), with different reported durations and a verse about the Spirit and angels; (3) the flying of the books (taṭāyur al-kutub), with verses about the book given in the right hand and the spread-open book; (4) the questioning (al-mas'ala), with verses commanding to stop and question; (5) the testimony of the ten witnesses (shahādat al-shuhūd al-‘ashara), including body parts, time, and guardian angels, with supporting Quranic verses and a hadith; (6) the terror of the change of colors (taghayyur al-alwān) of faces, with verses describing bright and dark faces; (7) the terror of the proclamation (al-munādāh) of happiness or misery by angels at the scale. Each item is supported by explicit scriptural evidence. The passage demonstrates that these events are real and form a necessary part of Islamic eschatological belief.

Key Terms
محاسبة
هول الوقوف
تطاير الكتب
مسألة
شهادة الشهود
تغير الألوان
مناداة
ميزان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These terrors are symbolic or allegorical and not literal.
Correction: The author explicitly states they are possible matters confirmed by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, making belief in their literal reality obligatory.

Checkpoint
What is the first terror listed by the author among the horrors of the Day of Judgment?
A) The standing (hawl al-wuqūf)
B) The accounting (muḥāsaba)
C) The flying of books (taṭāyur al-kutub)
D) The testimony of witnesses (shahādat al-shuhūd)

Key Takeaway
The Day of Judgment includes multiple terrors scripturally attested, all of which must be believed as literal realities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the seven terrors described in this lesson strikes the deepest fear in your heart? What does your current lifestyle reveal about how seriously you take that terror? Name one specific change you will make starting today to prepare for it.
?
The passage teaches that your own tongue, hands, and feet will testify against you. Is there any area of your life where you are living in a way that you would be ashamed for these witnesses to expose? What secret sin do you need to confess and leave right now, before that Day arrives?
?
You will be questioned about everything—even the use of your time, as the night and day testify. Consider your last 24 hours: which moments would you regret if they were brought to account? What will you do differently for the rest of today to ensure your testimony is in your favor?

Wisdom of the Terrors and Safety of the Righteous
The author explains the wisdom of the terrors and their impact on prophets and saints.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wisdom behind the terrors of the Day of Judgment and why the prophets and saints are safe from them according to Sunni theology.

Core Idea
The terrors of the Day are not for terrorizing the righteous, but for manifesting ranks and encouraging goodness.

One might wonder why the Day of Judgment involves such terrors if Allah already knows all. This lesson explores the wisdom behind those terrors and specifically addresses whether the prophets and saints are affected by them. The author presents a reasoned view supported by Quranic verses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the passage and locate the author's statement of the wisdom behind the terrors. Notice how he justifies the need for manifestation of ranks even though Allah is all-knowing.
The author mentions two aspects: manifestation of ranks and encouragement/deterrence.
2
Explore the supporting evidence
Look at the two Quranic verses quoted at the end. Understand their meaning and how they support the conclusion that the righteous are safe.
The verses promise 'no fear' and 'no grief' for the friends of Allah.
3
Assess the hesitation and conclusion
Notice the author's initial hesitation (taraddud) and how he resolves to the apparent view (al-ẓāhir) of safety. Consider why this view is considered apparent.
The hesitation suggests scholarly disagreement, but the author leans toward safety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحكمة في هذه المحاسبة والأهوال مع أن المحاسب خبير والناقد بصير ظهور مراتب أرباب الكمال، وفضائح أصحاب النقصان على رؤوس الأشهاد زيادة في لذات هؤلاء ومسراتهم. وآلام أولئك وأحزانهم، ثم في هذا ترغيب في الحسنات وزجر عن السيئات وهل يظهر أثر هذه الأهوال في الأنبياء والأولياء، والصلحاء والأتقياء؟ فيه تردد والظاهر السلامة : تتنزل عليهم الملائكة أن لا تخافوا ولا تحزنوا (٦) و ألا إن أولياء الله لا خوف عليهم ولاهم يحزنون ) (۷)
And the wisdom behind this accounting and terrors, despite the fact that the Accountant is All-Knowing and the Examiner is All-Seeing, is the manifestation of the ranks of the people of perfection and the exposure of the faults of the people of deficiency before the heads of the assembly, increasing the pleasures and joys of these and the pains and sorrows of those. Moreover, in this there is encouragement towards good deeds and deterrence from evil deeds. And does the effect of these terrors appear upon the prophets, the saints, the righteous, and the pious? There is hesitation regarding it, but the apparent view is safety: 'The angels descend upon them: Fear not nor grieve' (6) and 'Verily the friends of Allah, no fear is upon them nor do they grieve' (7).
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage provides the rationale (ḥikma) for the accounting and the terrors. The author states that even though Allah the Accountant is already fully aware and the Examiner (an-nāqid) is all-seeing, the purpose is to manifest the ranks of the people of perfection (arbāb al-kamāl, i.e., the believers) and to expose the faults of the people of deficiency (aṣḥāb an-nuqṣān, i.e., the disbelievers) in front of all witnesses (rū'ūs al-ashhād). This manifestation increases the pleasures and joys of the former and the pains and sorrows of the latter. Additionally, it serves as encouragement (targhīb) towards good deeds and deterrence (zajr) from evil deeds. The passage then raises the question of whether these terrors affect the prophets, saints, righteous, and pious. There is hesitation (taraddud), but the apparent view (aẓ-ẓāhir) is that they are safe (as-salāma). The author supports this with the Quranic verse: 'The angels descend upon them: Fear not nor grieve' and the verse: 'Verily the friends of Allah, no fear is upon them nor do they grieve.' Thus, the righteous are protected from the terror of that day.

Key Terms
حكمة
ترغيب
زجر
أنبياء
أولياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that even prophets and saints will be terrified on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: The author clarifies that the apparent view is that they are safe, as indicated by Quranic verses promising no fear or grief for the friends of Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the apparent view regarding the effect of these terrors on prophets and saints?
A) They will experience great fear
B) They are safe from them
C) They will be tested
D) They will be overwhelmed

Key Takeaway
The apparent view is that the prophets and saints are safe from the terrors of the Day, as supported by Quranic verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate the terrors of that Day, do you see yourself among the people of perfection or the people of deficiency? What concrete evidence from your life today supports that? Commit to one action that will solidify your rank.
?
The author says the terrors are to encourage good and deter evil. Think of a moment this week when you hesitated to do good or were tempted by evil. Did the reality of the Day of Judgment cross your mind? If not, what will you do to make that reality more present in your daily choices?
?
The prophets and saints are safe. How does knowing that the friends of Allah have no fear affect your desire to become closer to Him? Name one concrete step you will take this week to strengthen your friendship with Allah so that you may also be among those who are safe.

The Witnessing of Limbs and Days
Sanusi describes the witnessing of limbs and days as an eschatological terror.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine that body parts and even time itself bear witness on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
On Judgment Day, every limb and every day will testify against us.

This passage introduces one of the many eschatological terrors: the witnessing of limbs and the testimony of days and nights. The author cites Quranic verses and a hadith to establish that not only the angels but also one's own body and the days themselves will bear witness. This reinforces personal accountability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the three types of witness: limbs, days/nights, and the driver/witness.
The first word 'ما جلؤوها' is a corruption of 'يوم تشهد'.
2
Identify the Quranic verse about limbs
Find the verse that says their hearing, sight, and skins bear witness. Understand that this is a literal testimony.
3
Consider the hadith about days and nights
The hadith says each day and night testifies. What does that imply about our actions? Reflect on accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما جلؤوها شهد عليهم سمعهم وأبصارهم وجلودهم بما كانوا يعملون وقال : ما من يوم وليلة يأتي على ابن آدم إلا قال: أنا ليل جديد، وأنا فيما يُعمل في شهيد. وكذا قال في اليوم، وقال الله تعالى : وجاءت كل نفس معها سائق وشهيد. وهول تغير الألوان، قال الله تعالى : ( يوم تبيض وجوه وتسود وجوه ) وقال: ﴿ وجوه يومئذ مسفرة ضاحكة مستبشرة و وجوه يومئذ عليها غبرة ترهقها قترة ﴾ . وهول المناداة بالسعادة والشقاوة. وقال عليه السلام يكون عند كل كفة الميزان ملك، فإذا ترجح كفة الخير نادى ألا إن فلاناً سعد سعادة لا شقاوة بعدها أبداً. وإذا ترجح الكفة الأخرى، نادى الملك الثاني : ألا إن فلاناً شقي شقاوة لا سعادة بعدها أبداً. والحكمة في هذه المحاسبة والأهوال مع أن المحاسب خبير والناقد بصير ظهور مراتب أرباب الكمال، وفضائح أصحاب النقصان على رؤوس الأشهاد زيادة في لذات هؤلاء ومسراتهم. وآلام أولئك وأحزانهم، ثم في هذا ترغيب في الحسنات وزجر عن السيئات وهل يظهر أثر هذه الأهوال في الأنبياء والأولياء، والصلحاء والأتقياء؟ فيه تردد والظاهر السلامة : تتنزل عليهم الملائكة أن لا تخافوا ولا تحزنوا و ألا إن أولياء الله لا خوف عليهم ولاهم يحزنون
What they covered? Their hearing, their sight, and their skins bore witness against them of what they used to do. And he said: There is no day and night that comes upon the son of Adam except that it says: I am a new night, and I am a witness to what is done in me. And likewise he said concerning the day. And Allah Almighty said: And every soul came with it a driver and a witness. And there is the terror of the change of colors; Allah Almighty said: (On the day when faces become white and faces become black) and He said: (Faces on that day are bright, laughing, rejoicing, and faces on that day have upon them dust, overspread with darkness). And there is the proclamation of happiness and misery. And he, peace be upon him, said: At each pan of the scale there is an angel; when the pan of good outweighs, he calls out: Verily so-and-so has attained happiness after which there is no misery ever. And when the other pan outweighs, the second angel calls out: Verily so-and-so has become miserable with a misery after which there is no happiness ever. And the wisdom in this reckoning and these terrors, even though the Reckoner is all-knowing and the Critic is all-seeing, is the manifestation of the ranks of the people of perfection and the disgrace of the people of deficiency before the witnesses, as an increase in the delights and joys of these and the pains and sorrows of those. Then in this there is encouragement towards good deeds and deterrence from evil deeds. And does the effect of these terrors appear upon the prophets, the saints, the righteous, and the pious? There is hesitation about it, and the apparent is safety: The angels descend upon them saying: Do not fear and do not grieve, and: Verily the friends of Allah have no fear upon them nor do they grieve.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage enumerates several eschatological states (ahwal) of the Day of Judgment. First, it mentions the witnessing of the body parts (shahadat al-jawarih) against the sinners, citing a Quranic verse (41:20) though the printed text has a corruption. Then it refers to a hadith that each day and night testifies to what is done in it, and then the verse about every soul coming with a driver and witness (Qaf 50:21). Next is the terror of the change of colors (taghayyur al-alwan), with verses about faces becoming white or black (Al Imran 3:106) and faces being bright or dusty (Abasa 80:38-41). Then comes the proclamation (munada) of happiness or misery, supported by a hadith that at each pan of the scale (kifat al-mizan) there is an angel who proclaims the final state. The author then explains the wisdom (hikma) behind all these terrors: although Allah is already all-knowing, the public display of the ranks of the perfect and the deficiencies of the deficient increases the joy of the former and the sorrow of the latter, and also serves as incentive and deterrent. Finally, a question is raised: Do these terrors affect the prophets, saints, righteous, and pious? The author notes hesitation (taraddud) but states that the apparent (al-zahir) view is safety (salamah), citing verses from Surah Fussilat (41:30) and Surah Yunus (10:62) that the angels descend upon them with reassurance.

Key Terms
شهادة الجوارح
الشهيد
السائق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think only angels record deeds.
Correction: The Quran says body parts themselves testify.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following bears witness against a person?
A) Only the angels
B) Their own limbs
C) Their family
D) Their wealth

Key Takeaway
Your own body and even time itself will be witnesses against you.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which limb—your tongue, your eyes, your ears, or your hands—would you most fear testifying against you tomorrow, and what concrete step will you take tonight to ensure it speaks fewer sins?
?
If every passing night is a witness that will speak of your deeds, how will you choose to spend this very night differently than you had planned?
?
Imagine your driver (sā'iq) and your witness (shahīd) are now standing beside you. What would they say about your readiness for the encounter with your Lord, and what will you do right now to change that answer?

The Change of Faces and the Proclamation of Happiness or Misery
Sanusi describes two terrors: change of facial colors and proclamation of happiness/misery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two eschatological events: the change of facial colors and the angelic proclamation of one's final fate.

Core Idea
On that Day, faces will light up or darken, and angels will announce our eternal destiny.

This passage presents two powerful images of the Day of Judgment: the visible transformation of faces to white or black, and the angelic proclamation at the scales. Both serve as public declarations of one's spiritual state. The author cites Quran and hadith to ground these events.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses about faces
Notice the two categories: faces white/bright vs faces black/dusty. This is a literal change.
2
Read the hadith about the scales
Each scale has an angel who proclaims the outcome. Understand the two proclamations.
3
Reflect on the public nature
These are not private; they are witnessed by all. Why?

The Wisdom Behind the Terrors and the Safety of the Righteous
Sanusi explains the wisdom behind eschatological terrors and discusses their effect on the righteous.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
The terrors serve to heighten joy and sorrow, and the righteous are likely shielded from them.

After describing the terrors, the author turns to their wisdom: why does Allah make them public even though He already knows all? The answer is to increase the delight of the righteous and the shame of the wicked, and to encourage good deeds. Then a question arises: do these terrors affect even the prophets and saints? The author mentions hesitation but leans towards safety.

And there is the proclamation of happiness and misery. And he, peace be upon him, said: At each pan of the scale there is an angel; when the pan of good outweighs, he calls out: Verily so-and-so has attained happiness after which there is no misery ever. And when the other pan outweighs, the second angel calls out: Verily so-and-so has become miserable with a misery after which there is no happiness ever. And the wisdom in this reckoning and these terrors, even though the Reckoner is all-knowing and the Critic is all-seeing, is the manifestation of the ranks of the people of perfection and the disgrace of the people of deficiency before the witnesses, as an increase in the delights and joys of these and the pains and sorrows of those. Then in this there is encouragement towards good deeds and deterrence from evil deeds. And does the effect of these terrors appear upon the prophets, the saints, the righteous, and the pious? There is hesitation about it, and the apparent is safety: The angels descend upon them saying: Do not fear and do not grieve, and: Verily the friends of Allah have no fear upon them nor do they grieve.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage enumerates several eschatological states (ahwal) of the Day of Judgment. First, it mentions the witnessing of the body parts (shahadat al-jawarih) against the sinners, citing a Quranic verse (41:20) though the printed text has a corruption. Then it refers to a hadith that each day and night testifies to what is done in it, and then the verse about every soul coming with a driver and witness (Qaf 50:21). Next is the terror of the change of colors (taghayyur al-alwan), with verses about faces becoming white or black (Al Imran 3:106) and faces being bright or dusty (Abasa 80:38-41). Then comes the proclamation (munada) of happiness or misery, supported by a hadith that at each pan of the scale (kifat al-mizan) there is an angel who proclaims the final state. The author then explains the wisdom (hikma) behind all these terrors: although Allah is already all-knowing, the public display of the ranks of the perfect and the deficiencies of the deficient increases the joy of the former and the sorrow of the latter, and also serves as incentive and deterrent. Finally, a question is raised: Do these terrors affect the prophets, saints, righteous, and pious? The author notes hesitation (taraddud) but states that the apparent (al-zahir) view is safety (salamah), citing verses from Surah Fussilat (41:30) and Surah Yunus (10:62) that the angels descend upon them with reassurance.

Key Terms
الحكمة
المحاسبة
الأهوال
السلامة
الأنبياء
الأولياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think even prophets must experience all terrors.
Correction: The passage leans towards their safety.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the apparent view regarding the effect of terrors on the prophets and saints?
A) They experience them fully
B) They are safe from them
C) They experience them partially
D) It is unknown

Key Takeaway
The terrors have wisdom, and the righteous are likely shielded from them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The terrors are meant to manifest ranks and increase joy for the righteous and pain for the wicked. Are you living a life that would place you among the people of perfection? What specific action can you take today to ensure that on that day you are among those greeted by angels saying 'Do not fear'?
?
The passage emphasizes that the righteous are likely safe from these terrors. Does your current state of faith give you confidence that you will be among those who are safe? If not, what step will you take tonight to strengthen your relationship with Allah so that you become one of His friends?
?
The wisdom includes encouragement to good deeds and deterrence from evil. When you think about the terrors of the Day of Judgment, does it actually motivate you to change your behavior right now, or have you become numb to these reminders? What is one sin you will abandon today because of this lesson?

The Sirat: Bridge Over Hell and Its Interpretation
Defines the Sirat, refutes Mu'tazila, and offers alternative interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the traditional Sunni belief about the Sirat as a physical bridge over Hell, the Mu'tazila objections, and how scholars reconcile the apparent impossibility with God's power.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a real bridge, yet God's power makes crossing easy for believers.

In this passage, the author defines the Sirat as a bridge over Hell, citing hadith and Quran. He then addresses the Mu'tazila denial, presenting their arguments and offering a response based on God's omnipotence and the concept of violation of custom. The lesson shows how traditional theology upholds physical realities while allowing for miraculous ease.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. This will give you an overview of the argument.
Pay attention to how the passage moves from definition to objection to answer.
2
Identify the three main sections
The passage has a clear structure: definition of the Sirat, Mu'tazila objections and alternative interpretations, and the refutation. Identify each section in the Arabic.
The objection begins with 'وأنكره القاضي عبد الجبار' and the answer with 'والجواب'.
3
Understand the key concepts
Notice the terms 'مخالفة العادة' (violation of custom) and 'الورود' (passing over). These are central to the argument.
The hadith about different speeds of crossing shows God's ability to ease the path.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها الصراط، وهو جسر ممدود على متن جهنم ، يرده الأولون والآخرون أدق من الشعر، وأحد من السيف على ما ورد في الحديث الصحيح . ويشبه أن يكون المرور عليه هو المراد بورود كل أحد النار على ما قال تعالى: (وإن منكم إلا واردها) وأنكره القاضي عبد الجبار وكثير من المعتزلة زعماً منهم أنه لا يمكن الخطور عليه . ولو أمكن ففيه تعذيب، ولا عذاب على المؤمنين والصلحاء يوم القيامة . قالوا : بل المراد به طريق الجنة المشار إليه بقوله تعالى. سيهديهم ويصلح بالهم ) وطريق النار المشار إليه بقوله : ( فاهدوهم إلى صراط الجحيم ) وقيل : المراد الأدلة الواضحة ، وقيل : العبادات كالصلاة والزكاة، ونحوهما. وقيل : الأعمال الردية التي يسأل عنها ويؤاخذ بها، كأنه يمر عليها ويطول المرور بكثرتها، ويقصر بقلتها. والجواب - أن إمكان العبور ظاهر كالمشي على الماء، والطيران في الهواء غايته مخالفة العادة . ثم الله تعالى يسهل الطريق على من أراد، كما جاء في الحديث أن منهم من هو كالبرق الخاطف ومنهم من هو كالريح الهابة، ومنهم من هو كالجواد، ومنهم من تخور رجلاه وتتعلق يداه ومنهم من يخر على وجهه .
And among them is the Sirat, which is a bridge extended over the surface of Hell; the first and the last will pass over it, finer than a hair and sharper than a sword, as reported in the authentic hadith. And it appears that crossing over it is what is meant by the 'entry' (wurud) of everyone into the Fire, as Allah Almighty said: (And there is none of you but will pass over it [wurud]) And Qadi Abd al-Jabbar and many of the Mu'tazila denied this, claiming that it is not possible to pass over it. And if it were possible, it would involve punishment, and there is no punishment for the believers and the righteous on the Day of Resurrection. They said: Rather, what is meant by it is the path to Paradise referred to in His statement: He will guide them and set their affairs right, and the path to the Fire referred to in His statement: (So lead them to the path of Hell) And it was said: what is meant is the clear proofs, and it was said: the acts of worship like prayer, zakat, and the like. And it was said: the evil deeds about which one is asked and taken to account, as if one passes over them; the crossing is long due to their abundance and short due to their scarcity. And the answer is that the possibility of crossing is apparent, like walking on water and flying in the air; its ultimate is violation of custom. Then Allah Almighty makes the path easy for whomsoever He wills, as came in the hadith that among them is one who is like a lightning flash, and among them is one who is like the blowing wind, and among them is one who is like a horse, and among them there is one whose legs fail and his hands cling, and among them there is one who falls on his face.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage discusses the Sirat (صراط), which is the bridge over Hell. It begins by defining it: a bridge stretched over the surface of Hell, thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword, based on a sound hadith. The author notes that crossing this bridge is likely the interpretation of the Quranic verse 'And there is none of you but will pass over it (wurud)' (Maryam 19:71). The Mu'tazila, led by Qadi Abd al-Jabbar, objected: (1) crossing such a fine and sharp object is impossible; (2) even if possible, it would cause pain, and believers must not be punished. They offered alternative interpretations: the 'entry' (wurud) means the path to Paradise or the path to Hell (as per other verses), or it refers to clear proofs (adilla wadiha), or acts of worship (like prayer and zakat), or even evil deeds that one reviews and is held accountable for—the length of crossing varies with the quantity of deeds. The author then gives the answer (jawab): crossing such a bridge is possible as a violation of custom (mukhalafat al-‘ada), just like walking on water or flying in the air. Moreover, Allah makes the crossing easy for some believers, as described in a hadith detailing different speeds of crossing, from lightning-fast to falling on one's face. Thus, the physical reality of the Sirat is affirmed while acknowledging God's power to facilitate passage.

Key Terms
الصراط
الجسر
الورود
مخالفة العادة
القاضي عبد الجبار
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believed that a physical bridge over Hell is impossible and would cause unjust punishment for believers.
Correction: The Sunni response affirms that God's power can make the crossing possible and painless, as a miracle (mukhalafat al-ada).

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Mu'tazila gave for denying that the Sirat is a physical bridge over Hell?
A) It contradicts the Quran
B) Passing over it is impossible, and if possible it would cause punishment which believers do not deserve
C) The hadith about it is weak
D) It is mentioned only in the Torah

Key Takeaway
The Sirat is a real bridge over Hell, but God's power makes crossing possible and varied for believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadith describes believers crossing the Sirat at different speeds—some like lightning, some falling on their faces. Which category do you fear you might belong to, and what specific sin or attachment in your life right now could be slowing you down? How will you cut it loose today?
?
If you truly believed that Allah can make the impossible possible—like walking on water or crossing a razor-thin bridge over Hell—what one area of your life would you stop trying to control and finally surrender to Him? What is stopping you from doing that right now?
?
The Mu'tazila denied the physical Sirat because they couldn't reconcile it with their reason. Where in your own faith are you tempted to rationalize away something Allah has clearly promised? Will you trust His word over your logic, even if it seems impossible?

The Reality of the Scale (Mizan) on the Day of Judgment
Affirms the physical scale with two pans, tongue, and legs, refuting Mu'tazila denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural basis for the literal physical scale on the Day of Judgment and the position of the majority of commentators against Mu'tazila denial.

Core Idea
The scale of deeds is a real, physical instrument with two pans, tongue, and legs.

In this passage, the author affirms the reality of the Mizan, the scale on which deeds are weighed on the Day of Resurrection. He cites Quranic verses and the consensus of most commentators (mufassirun) that the scale is a literal physical object with specific parts. This directly counters the metaphorical interpretations of the Mu'tazila. Let's dive into the evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and literal translation to get the plain meaning without analysis.
Notice the two Quranic verses quoted.
2
Identify the scriptural evidence
Note the two Quranic verses and the hadith reference that support the literal scale.
The hadith is mentioned but not quoted.
3
Contrast the two positions
Understand why many commentators take the scale literally (imkan) and why some Mu'tazila deny it.
The author sides with the literalists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها الميزان قال الله تعالى ونضع الموازين القسط ليوم القيامة) وقال : فأما من ثقلت موازينه فهو في عيشة راضية وأما من خفت موازينه فأمه هاوية ) . ذهب كثير من المفسرين إلى أنه ميزان له كفتان ولسان وساقان، عملاً بالحقيقة لإمكانها، وقد ورد في الحديث تفسيره بذلك وأنكره بعض المعتزلة
And among them is the Scale (Mizan). Allah Almighty said: And We shall set up the scales of justice for the Day of Resurrection. And He said: Then as for him whose scales are heavy, he will have a pleasant life; and as for him whose scales are light, his abode will be the abyss. Many of the commentators (mufassirun) held that it is a scale having two pans, a tongue, and two legs, acting according to literal meaning because it is possible, and its interpretation with that has come in the hadith, and some of the Mu'tazila denied it.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage addresses the Scale (Mizan) of deeds. It begins by citing two Quranic verses: one from Al-Anbiya (21:47) about setting up the scales of justice, and another from Al-Qari'a (101:6-8) about the heaviness or lightness of scales leading to pleasant life or the abyss. The author then states the position of many mufassirun (commentators): they take the scale literally (haqiqa) as a physical instrument with two pans (kifatayn), a tongue (lisan), and two legs (saqan), because such a thing is possible (imkan) and because it is described that way in hadith. On the other hand, some Mu'tazila denied this literal interpretation, presumably preferring a metaphorical understanding. The author does not elaborate their denial here but simply notes it. The passage affirms the literal, physical reality of the scale as a real object on the Day of Judgment.

Correction: The majority of Sunni commentators affirm it is a real physical scale with pans, tongue, and legs, based on scripture and hadith.

The Bridge over Hell: Reality and Mu'tazila Objection
Defense of the Bridge's literal reality against Mu'tazila objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine of the Bridge (الصراط) over Hell, the Mu'tazila objection to its literal crossing, and the theological response that affirms divine omnipotence through the suspension of natural laws.

Core Idea
The Bridge is real; crossing it is possible through Allah's power, not impossible despite miracles.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid presents a classic debate about the afterlife reality of the Bridge (الصراط). The author first describes it as sharper than a sword, then addresses the Mu'tazila denial that believers could cross it without suffering. Various alternative interpretations are mentioned before the definitive response rooted in Allah's ability to suspend natural laws.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally before you break it down.
Notice the shift from description to objection to response.
2
Identify the three main parts
The passage has three clear sections: the hadith description of the Bridge, the Mu'tazila objection with their alternative interpretations, and the author's response using divine omnipotence.
3
Examine the Mu'tazila objection and alternatives
The Mu'tazila claim crossing is impossible and would cause torment. They propose multiple alternative meanings for 'ورود'. Note each one.
They interpret 'ورود' as the path to Paradise or Hell, or as metaphors for proofs, acts, or deeds.
4
Understand the response
The author argues that crossing is possible as a violation of custom (kharq al-'ada), just like miracles. Allah makes it easy for believers.
This response relies on divine omnipotence, not natural causation.
5
Reflect on the doctrinal significance
Consider how this passage defends a literal afterlife event while addressing rational objections. It affirms both the Quran and hadith literally and God's absolute power.

Commentary
This passage discusses the Bridge (الصراط) over Hell, presenting objections from the Mu'tazila and providing a response. The author begins by stating that the Bridge is sharper than hair and a sword according to a sound hadith. Allah facilitates it for believers, as described in a hadith showing varying speeds of crossing. The passage affirms the literal reality of the Bridge while addressing theological concerns.

?
The author compares crossing the Bridge to walking on water—both are violations of natural custom. Do you truly believe that Allah is not bound by the laws He created? Where in your life do you limit Him by what you consider 'possible' or 'impossible'?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected the literal crossing because they thought it would cause torment, and they tried to protect believers from that fear. But the truth is that the crossing is real, and the ease of it depends on one's deeds. Are you living as if that crossing is real? The Balance (al-Mizan) and the Weighing of Deeds
Exposition of the Balance, objections of Mu'tazila, and answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the arguments surrounding the literal vs. metaphorical interpretation of the Balance (al-Mizan) and the responses to Mu'tazila objections.

Core Idea
The Balance is real, even if deeds are accidents; Allah can weigh them as He wills.

This passage delves into one of the eschatological realities: the Balance on the Day of Judgment. Several Quranic verses describe the weighing of deeds, and commentators have differed on its nature. Some take it literally, while others, especially the Mu'tazila, argue that deeds are accidents that cannot be weighed. The text presents these views and the responses offered by Sunni scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses and literal interpretation
Read the two Quranic verses and note how many mufassirs take the Balance literally with pans, tongue, and legs. Consider the hadith support.
The literal interpretation is based on possibility and prophetic tradition.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila objection
Identify the Mu'tazila argument that deeds are accidents (a'rad) that cease to exist, making physical weighing impossible. Recognize their metaphorical interpretation of justice.
This objection challenges the literal reading.
3
Explore the responses and alternative interpretations
Go through the answers given: weighing scrolls, deeds becoming luminous/dark bodies, and the explanation of the plural 'موازين' for exaltation or multiplicity of balances.
Each response upholds the reality of weighing while addressing the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها الميزان قال الله تعالى ونضع الموازين القسط ليوم القيامة) (٥) وقال : فأما من ثقلت موازينه فهو في عيشة راضية وأما من خفت موازينه فأمه هاوية ) (٦) . ذهب كثير من المفسرين إلى أنه ميزان له كفتان ولسان وساقان، عملاً بالحقيقة لإمكانها، وقد ورد في الحديث تفسيره بذلك وأنكره بعض المعتزلة ذهاباً إلى أن الأعمال أعراض لا يمكن وزنها ، فكيف إذا زالت وتلاشت؟ بل المراد به العدل الثابت في كل شيء، ولذا ذكره بلفظ الجمع، وإلا فالميزان المشهور واحد. وقيل: هو الإدراك . فميزان الألوان البصر، والأصوات السمع والطعوم الذوق، وكذا سائر الحواس. وميزان المعقولات العلم والعقل . وأجيب بأنه يوزن صحائف الأعمال. وقيل: بل تجعل الحسنات أجسامـاً نورانية، والسيئات أجساماً ظلمانية، وأما لفظ الجمع فللاستعظام، وقيل: لكل مكلف ميزان . وإنما الميزان الكبير واحد إظهاراً لجلالة الأمر وعظمة المقام
And among them is the Balance. Allah said: (And We set up the just scales for the Day of Resurrection) (5) and said: (Then as for him whose scales are heavy, he will be in a pleasant life, and as for him whose scales are light, his mother will be the Abyss) (6). Many commentators (mufassirun) have held that it is a balance with two pans, a tongue, and two legs, acting on the literal meaning due to its possibility, and that interpretation has come in the hadith. Some Mu'tazila denied it, claiming that deeds are accidents (a'rad) that cannot be weighed – how then when they have ceased and vanished? Rather, what is meant is the established justice in everything, and for that reason it was mentioned in the plural, otherwise the well-known balance is one. And it was said: it is perception. So the balance of colors is sight, of sounds is hearing, of tastes is taste, and likewise the rest of the senses; and the balance of intelligibles is knowledge and intellect. And it was answered that the scrolls of deeds are weighed. And it was said: rather good deeds become luminous bodies, and bad deeds become dark bodies. And as for the plural word, it is for exaltation. And it was said: for every accountable person there is a balance. And the great balance is but one, to manifest the majesty of the matter and the greatness of the station.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage treats the Balance (الميزان) as one of the eschatological realities. The author first cites Quranic verses about weighing deeds. He then reports that many exegetes take the Balance literally, with two pans, a tongue, and legs, based on its possibility and prophetic tradition. Some Mu'tazila reject this because actions are accidents (a'rad) that cease to exist and thus cannot be weighed; they interpret it metaphorically as justice. Alternative interpretations are given: balance as perception for various faculties, or as scrolls of deeds, or good and bad deeds becoming luminous/dark bodies. The plural 'موازين' is explained as exaltation or as each person having a balance, while the single great balance manifests the matter's grandeur. The passage balances literal acceptance with interpretive responses to objections.

Key Terms
الميزان
الأعراض
صحائف الأعمال
الحسنات
السيئات
مفسرون
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Balance is only a metaphor for justice and not a real physical scale.
Correction: The passage shows that many scholars take it literally, and responses address the objection by explaining how deeds can be weighed even if they are accidents.

Checkpoint
What was the main objection of the Mu'tazila regarding the Balance?
A) The Balance is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Deeds are accidents that cannot be weighed after they vanish.
C) The Balance is only for angels, not humans.
D) The Balance contradicts reason because it has two pans.

Key Takeaway
The Balance is a real eschatological entity whose literal interpretation is upheld against Mu'tazila objections through various plausible explanations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the scroll of your deeds were placed on the Balance right now, would the pan of good deeds outweigh the bad? What one deed from today would you want to add to the heavy side before you sleep?
?
The Mu'tazila saw a difficulty in weighing deeds because they vanish. But you know your deeds are recorded. Are you living as though your every action is being stored for a literal weighing, or do you treat some deeds as too small to matter?
?
The plural 'mawazin' is for exaltation and grandeur. Do you truly exalt the Day of Judgment in your heart, or have you reduced it to a distant, abstract event? What would change in your life if you felt the weight of that Day now?

The Prophet's Pond (al-Hawd) and Its Description
Description of the Prophet's Pond and its eschatological role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality and significance of the Prophet's Pond (al-Hawd) as an eschatological event, including its description and the sequence of finding the Prophet on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
The Prophet's Pond is a real, described place where believers will drink and never thirst.

In this lesson, we explore one of the eschatological realities affirmed by Sunni scholars: the Prophet's Pond (al-Hawd). Drawing from the Quranic reference to al-Kawthar and a detailed hadith, we learn about its vast size and blessings. Additionally, a tradition from the Companions reveals the sequence of where to find the Prophet on the Day of Resurrection, emphasizing the Pond as a key location.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the Quranic verse and hadith
The passage begins with a Quranic verse about al-Kawthar. Then it quotes a hadith describing the Pond. Notice how both are used as evidence.
3
Note the physical attributes of the Pond
The hadith gives five attributes: size (a month's journey), equal corners, water whiter than milk, fragrance better than musk, and cups more numerous than stars. Also the promise of never thirsting.
These details affirm the Pond's physical reality.
4
Understand the sequence of finding the Prophet
The Companions ask where to find the Prophet on Judgment Day. He responds: first on the Bridge, then at the Balance, then at the Pond. This shows the order of eschatological events.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the Pond is important: it is a reward for believers, a place of meeting the Prophet, and a source of eternal satisfaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها الحوض . قال تعالى : إنا أعطيناك الكوثر (١) . وفي الحديث: «حوضي مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيض من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكيزانه أكثر من نجوم السماء، من شرب منها فلا يظمأ أبداً». وقال الصحابة له عليه (السلام أين نطلبك يوم الحشر؟ فقال: على الصراط . فإن لم تجدوا فعلى الميزان فإن لم تجدوا فعلى الحوض.
And among them is the Pond. He said: (Indeed, We have given you al-Kawthar) (1). And in the hadith: 'My Pond is a month's journey, its corners are equal, its water is whiter than milk, its fragrance is more pleasant than musk, its cups are more numerous than the stars of the sky; whoever drinks from it will never thirst again.' And the Companions said to him (peace be upon him): 'Where shall we seek you on the Day of Gathering?' He said: 'On the Bridge. If you do not find me, then at the Balance. If you do not find me, then at the Pond.'
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage briefly presents the Pond (الحوض) of the Prophet Muhammad as another eschatological reality. It begins by citing the Quranic verse about al-Kawthar, often interpreted as the Pond. Then it quotes a hadith describing the Pond's vast size (a month's journey), its equal corners, its water and fragrance, and the abundance of cups. The hadith emphasizes that whoever drinks from it will never thirst. Finally, it narrates a tradition where the Companions ask the Prophet where to find him on the Day of Resurrection, and he replies they should seek him first on the Bridge, then at the Balance, then at the Pond. This underscores the sequential eschatological events and the Prophet's presence at each stage.

Key Terms
الحوض
الكوثر
الصراط
الميزان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: The Pond is merely symbolic or metaphorical, not a real physical entity.
Correction: The text affirms its physical reality: it has a specific size (a month's journey), physical attributes (water, fragrance), and cups. The hadith describes it concretely, indicating it is a real place.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, where should the Companions look for the Prophet on the Day of Gathering if they do not find him on the Bridge?
A) On the Bridge again.
B) At the Balance.
C) At the Pond.
D) In Paradise.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's Pond is a real, described eschatological blessing where believers will drink and find the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet described his Pond as having water whiter than milk and fragrance sweeter than musk. When you think of your greatest joys in this life, do they compare to this description? What does your heart truly long for?
?
On the Day of Gathering, the Prophet told the Companions they could find him at the Bridge, then the Balance, then the Pond. Are you actively seeking him now, or will you only look for him on that Day? What one thing will you do today to draw closer to his Sunnah?
?
The promise of the Pond is that whoever drinks from it will never thirst again. In your life, what are you thirsting for—status, love, security? How does this eternal quenching change what you prioritize starting tomorrow?

The Philosophers' Symbolic Interpretation of the Afterlife
The hukama' view that afterlife descriptions symbolize soul's states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the philosopher-theologians (hukama') interpret scriptural descriptions of Paradise and Hell as representations of spiritual states of the soul.

Core Idea
Heaven and Hell are spiritual states of the soul, depicted physically in revelation.

This lesson explores a distinctive interpretation of the afterlife offered by the 'verifiers among the philosophers' in Islamic theology. They argue that the detailed descriptions of Paradise and Hell in the Qur'an and hadith are not merely physical realities but symbolic representations (tamthil) of the soul's inner states of happiness or misery. This view seeks to reconcile scriptural imagery with philosophical psychology, affirming the soul's immortality and its ultimate felicity or suffering based on its virtues or defects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Carefully read the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice the key terms like 'tamthil' (representation) and 'taswir' (depiction).
The passage is incomplete; it cuts off mid-sentence.
2
Identify the core claim
The philosophers hold that the details of reward and punishment in the Law are representations of the ranks and states of souls. Understand that this is a symbolic interpretation.
3
Understand the rationale
Why do people not perceive this truth in the worldly life? Because of attachments and obstacles that vanish at death. This explains the need for symbolic descriptions.
The soul itself does not perish; it delights or suffers based on its perfection or deficiency.
4
Examine eternal misery
The passage specifies that misery is not eternal for all; only 'deeply ingrained compound ignorance' (al-jahl al-murakkab al-rasikh) leads to eternal suffering. Consider what this implies about divine mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الثامن - ذهب المحققون من الحكماء إلى أن ما ورد في الشرع من تفاصيل أحوال الجنة والنار، والثواب والعقاب تمثيل وتصوير لمراتب النفوس وأحوالها في السعادة والشقاوة ولذاتها وآلامها فإنها لا تفنى بل تبقى ملتذة بكمالاتها (٢) فذلك ثوابها وجنانها، أو متألمه بنقصانها ، فذلك عقابها ونيرانها، وإنما لم تتنبه لذلك في هذا العالم لما بها من العلائق والعوائق الزائلة بالمفارقة وليست شقاوتها سرمدية (۳) البتة، بل قد تتدرج من درجات الشقاوة إلى درجات السعادة وإنما الشقاوة السرمدية هي الجهل المركب الراسخ، والشرارة المضادة للملكة الفاضلة وتفصيل ذلك أن فوات كمال النفس يكون إما لأمر
He said: The eighth investigation - The verifiers among the philosophers (hukama') have held that what has come in the Law (al-shar') of details of the states of Paradise and Hell, and reward and punishment, is representation (tamthil) and depiction (taswir) of the ranks of souls and their states in happiness and misery, and their pleasures and pains. For they (the souls) do not perish but remain delighting in their perfections – that is their reward and their gardens; or suffering from their deficiencies – that is their punishment and their fires. And they do not realize this in this world due to the attachments and obstacles that vanish upon separation (from the body). And their misery is not eternal at all, but they may gradually progress from degrees of misery to degrees of happiness. Eternal misery is only the deeply ingrained compound ignorance (al-jahl al-murakkab al-rasikh) and the evil opposite of the virtuous disposition. And the detail of that is that the loss of the soul's perfection is either due to a matter...
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage begins the eighth investigation of the work, presenting the view of the 'verifiers among the philosophers' (المحققون من الحكماء). They interpret the scriptural descriptions of Paradise and Hell, reward and punishment, as symbolic representations (تمثيل وتصوير) of the inner states of souls – their ranks in happiness or misery, pleasures or pains. The soul does not perish; after death it either delights in its perfections (its reward) or suffers from its deficiencies (its punishment). The reason people do not perceive this in the worldly life is due to bodily attachments and obstacles that disappear at death. Importantly, misery is not eternal for all; souls can move from misery to happiness through gradual progression. Permanent misery is only the case of 'compound ignorance' (الجهل المركب) that is deeply rooted, and the evil opposed to virtuous character. The passage then begins to elaborate that loss of perfection occurs either due to... (text cuts off). This philosophical interpretation emphasizes spiritual realities over purely physical descriptions, while still affirming the soul's immortality and ultimate happiness or misery.

Key Terms
المحققون
الحكماء
التمثيل
التصوير
السعادة
الشقاوة
الجهل المركب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the philosophers deny physical resurrection and reject scriptural descriptions as mere metaphors.
Correction: The philosophers affirm spiritual realities and interpret the descriptions as symbolic representations, not literal falsehoods. They believe in reward and punishment but as soul's states.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers (hukama'), what is eternal misery?
A) Any suffering in Hell.
B) The deeply ingrained compound ignorance.
C) Physical torment.
D) Separation from God.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers interpret Paradise and Hell as spiritual states of the soul, with eternal misery confined to deeply ingrained compound ignorance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the descriptions of Paradise and Hell are symbols of the soul's spiritual states. If you were to die right now, which state would your soul be in: delight from its perfections or pain from its deficiencies? Be honest—and then ask yourself what attachments are preventing you from realizing this truth today.
?
The passage warns of 'deeply ingrained compound ignorance' as the cause of eternal misery. What is one belief you hold that you have never questioned, but which might be false? Will you investigate it, or remain in ignorance?
?
The philosophers say that misery is not eternal except for those with compound ignorance. Do you live as if you have infinite time to perfect your soul, or as if every moment counts? Commit to one specific action today to increase your soul's perfection.
