Consensus on Eternity and the Philosophical Objection
Consensus statement, then objection-and-answer about bodily finitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic consensus on the eternal duration of Paradise and Hell, and how the objection based on finite bodily powers is answered by appealing to God's omnipotence and the possibility of recreation.

Core Idea
Eternity of reward and punishment depends on God's power, not on natural durability.

This passage presents the Muslim consensus on the eternal duration of both Paradise and Hell. It then anticipates a philosophical objection: how can a finite body endure eternal punishment? The answer is not to argue for the body's natural endurance, but to point to God's power to recreate and sustain.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the strong opening consensus statement, then the three-part objection, and finally the concise answer.
The objection begins with 'فإن قيل' and the answer with 'قلنا'.
2
Identify the logical structure
The passage has three clear sections: consensus, objection (three points), and answer (two parts). See how the answer first rejects the premises, then provides a positive alternative.
3
Analyze the answer's strategy
The answer does not argue for natural immortality of the body. Instead, it shifts to divine omnipotence: God can create a replacement (badal). Find the Qur'anic verse used as proof.
The verse is from Surah an-Nisa (4:56) about replacing skins.
4
Reflect on theological implications
Consider why this answer is important: it grounds eschatology in God's power rather than philosophical assumptions about nature.
This shows the priority of revelation and divine will over rational speculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجمع المسلمون على خلود أهل الجنة في الجنة، وخلود الكفار في النار. فإن قيل : القوى الجسمانية متناهية، فلا تقبل خلود الحياة، وأيضاً الرطوبة التي مادة الحياة تفنى بالحرارة، سيما حرارة نار الجحيم، فتفنى إلى الفناء ضرورة، وأيضاً دوام الإحراق مع بقاء الحياة خروج عن قضية العقل. هي قلنا: هذه قواعد فلسفية غير مسلمة عند المليين، ولا صحيحة عند القائلين بإسناد الحوادث إلى القادر المختار وعلى تقدير تناهي القوى وزوال الحياة يجوز أن يخلق الله البدل ، فيدوم الثواب والعقاب . قال الله تعالى: كلما نضجت جلودهم بدلناهم جلوداً غيرها ليذوقوا العذاب (۱)
The Muslims are agreed on the eternity of the people of Paradise in Paradise, and the eternity of the disbelievers in the Fire. For if it is said: bodily powers are finite, so they do not accept eternal life; also, the moisture which is the material of life is consumed by heat, especially the heat of the fire of Hell, so it necessarily perishes to annihilation; also, the continuation of burning while life remains is a departure from rational judgment. (We say:) These are philosophical principles not conceded by the people of the [divine] law (milliyyun), nor correct for those who attribute events to the Omnipotent Chooser. And assuming the finitude of powers and the cessation of life, it is possible that Allah creates a replacement, so reward and punishment continue. Allah the Exalted said: "Whenever their skins are roasted, We replace them with other skins so that they may taste the punishment." (1)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the consensus of Muslims that the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell are eternal. It then presents an objection based on philosophical premises: bodily powers are finite and cannot sustain eternal life; moisture, the basis of life, is consumed by heat, especially Hellfire; and the idea of continuous burning with life is rationally untenable. The answer rejects these as philosophical principles not accepted by adherents of divine law and by those who attribute all events to the Omnipotent Chooser (al-Qadir al-Mukhtar). Even if powers end and life ceases, God can create a substitute to perpetuate reward and punishment, as the Qur'an states in verse 4:56 about replacing skins.

Key Terms
خلود
القوى الجسمانية
القادر المختار
البدل
نضجت جلودهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Eternal punishment is physically impossible because finite bodies cannot endure infinite torment.
Correction: The author does not claim bodies are naturally eternal. Instead, God's power allows Him to recreate the body as it perishes, so punishment continues.

Checkpoint
How does the author answer the objection that bodily powers are finite and cannot support eternal life in Hell?
A) The bodies of the damned are spiritual, not physical.
B) God can create a replacement body when the original is destroyed.
C) The heat of Hell is not real fire.
D) The objection is ignored as irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The eternity of reward and punishment is maintained by God's power to recreate, not by the inherent durability of the body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that your body will be replaced eternally to endure punishment in Hell, what would you change about your actions today?
?
The objection relies on human reasoning about natural limits. In what area of your life do you trust your own reasoning over God's clear statements in the Quran? What step can you take today to submit your mind to revelation?
?
The passage emphasizes God's absolute power to recreate. Does your daily life reflect a deep trust in God's ability to do what seems impossible? What is one area where you need to live this belief more?

Punishment of the Ignorant Disbeliever Who Sought Truth
Affirms punishment for those who fail to find truth despite effort, contra Jahiz and Anbari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that sincere effort in seeking truth does not automatically excuse disbelief, and why the dissenting view of Jahiz and Anbari is considered a breach of consensus.

Core Idea
Sincere search does not excuse disbelief; the texts and consensus hold firm.

This lesson addresses a specific theological debate: whether a person who genuinely seeks the truth but fails to find it is excused from punishment. The author firmly rejects the opinion of Jahiz and Anbari, using Qur'anic verses and consensus to argue that such a person is still accountable. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully to grasp the core argument.
Notice the strong language: 'breach of consensus' and 'abandonment of texts'.
2
Identify the two opposing positions
Note the author's position (punishment) and the dissenting view of al-Jahiz and al-‘Anbari (excused).
3
Examine the evidence cited
The author uses two Qur'anic verses and consensus. Understand how they are used to counter the dissenting argument.
Verses are about no hardship and no blame on the blind/lame; the author argues the perplexed have greater incapacity.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this issue matters for the broader theology of accountability and divine justice.
This debate touches on how we understand God's wisdom and mercy in relation to human effort.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا حكم الكافر الجاهل المعاند وكذا من بالغ في الطلب والنظر، واستفرغ المجهود ولم ينل المقصود خلافاً للجاحظ والعنبري، حيث زعما أنه معذور، إذ لا يليق بحكمة الحكيم أن يعذبه مع بذل الجهد والطاقة من غير جرم وتقصير. كيف وقد قال الله تعالى : وما جعل عليكم في الدين من حرج (۱) ليس على الأعمى حرج ولا على الأعرج حرج ولا على المريض حرج (۲) ولا شك أن عجز المتحير أشد . وهذا الفرق خرق للإجماع وترك للنصوص الواردة في هذا الباب.
This is the ruling concerning the ignorant defiant disbeliever (al-kafir al-jahil al-mu'anid), and likewise one who exerted himself in seeking and investigating, exhausted his effort, yet did not attain the goal, contrary to al-Jahiz and al-‘Anbari, who claimed he is excused, because it is not befitting the wisdom of the Wise to punish him while he exerted effort and energy without sin or shortcoming. How, when Allah the Exalted said: "And He has not placed upon you in religion any hardship" (1); "There is no blame upon the blind, nor upon the lame, nor upon the ill" (2); and there is no doubt that the incapacity of the perplexed is greater. This difference of opinion is a breach of consensus and abandonment of the texts that have come down in this chapter.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage states the position that the ignorant and obstinate disbeliever (al-kafir al-jahil al-mu'anid) is not excused, nor is the one who earnestly seeks the truth but fails to reach it. This opposes al-Jahiz and al-‘Anbari, who argue that such a person is excused because punishing him after he exerted effort would be unjust. The author counters by citing Qur'anic verses indicating that religion does not impose hardship, and that the blind and ill are exempted, implying that the perplexed person's incapacity is even greater—yet the correct position upholds punishment. The dissenting view is a breach of consensus (ijma') and a departure from relevant texts.

Key Terms
الكافر الجاهل المعاند
الطلب والنظر
المقصود
الحرج
المتحير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sincere effort in seeking truth excuses failure to accept Islam.
Correction: The author argues that even after exhausting effort, one is not excused; the dissenting view is a breach of consensus.

Checkpoint
What is the position of al-Jahiz and al-‘Anbari regarding one who sincerely seeks truth but fails?
A) He is still punished as a disbeliever.
B) He is excused and not punished.
C) He is treated as a Muslim.
D) His case is deferred to God's will.

Key Takeaway
Sincere search does not automatically excuse disbelief; the author upholds punishment and rejects the dissenting view as a breach of consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that your sincere efforts in searching for truth automatically exempt you from accountability? How does this lesson challenge that assumption in your own life?
?
When you face a difficult question in faith, do you tend to rely on your own reasoning or do you submit to the texts and consensus? What would it cost you to truly submit?
?
If you knew someone who claims to have sought truth but ended up with disbelief, would you treat them as excused or as accountable? How does this lesson change your responsibility toward them?

Three Views on the Fate of Polytheists' Children
Presents three scholarly views on children of polytheists in the afterlife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three scholarly opinions on the afterlife fate of children who die before reaching maturity, and the Qur'anic and hadith evidence used to support each view.

Core Idea
The fate of children of polytheists is debated among scholars based on divine justice and foreknowledge.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid presents three different positions regarding children of polytheists who die before maturity. The majority view, a Mu'tazilite view, and a third view based on divine foreknowledge are each supported by scriptural evidence. Understanding these positions reveals how different theological principles shape rulings on eschatological matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three views
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice that the passage presents three distinct opinions: the majority opinion, the Mu'tazilite opinion, and a third opinion based on divine foreknowledge.
The passage does not endorse any particular view; it simply presents them.
2
Examine the evidence for each view
For the majority, note the hadith about Khadija's children. For the Mu'tazila, note the Qur'anic verses about bearing burdens. For the third view, note the reliance on God's knowledge of what would have happened.
3
Consider the implications for divine justice
Reflect on why these different conclusions arise. The Mu'tazila emphasize God's justice, while the majority emphasize scriptural literalism. The third view attempts to reconcile justice with foreknowledge.
This connects to broader discussions of divine justice and predestination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا في حق الكفار عناداً واعتقاداً، وأما الكفار حكماً كأطفال المشركين، فكذلك عند الأكثرين لدخولهم في العمومات، ولما روي أن خديجة (رضي الله عنها) سألت النبي عليه السلام عن أطفالها الذين ماتوا في الجاهلية، فقال : هم في النار. وقالت المعتزلة، ومن تبعهم : لا يعذبون بل هم خدم أهل الجنة ، على ما ورد الحديث، لأن تعذيب من لا جرم له ظلم ولقوله: ﴿ ولا تزر وازرة وزر أخرى) (۱) ولا تجزون إلا ما كنتم تعملون ) (٢). ونحو ذلك . وقيل : من علم الله تعالى منه الإيمان والطاعة على تقدير البلوغ ففي الجنة، ومن علم منه الكفر والعصيان ففي النار.
This concerns the disbelievers out of obstinacy and belief. As for those who are disbelievers by legal ruling (hukman), such as the children of polytheists, they are likewise according to the majority, because they are included in the general [texts], and because of the report that Khadija (may Allah be pleased with her) asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about her children who died in the Jahiliyya, and he said: 'They are in the Fire.' The Mu'tazila and those who follow them said: 'They are not punished; rather they are servants of the people of Paradise, according to what has come in the hadith, because punishing one who has no sin is injustice, and because of His saying: "And no bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another" (1) and "You will not be recompensed except for what you used to do" (2), and similar [proofs]. And it was said: Whom Allah knows from him that he would have believed and obeyed had he reached maturity, he is in Paradise; and whom He knows from him disbelief and disobedience, he is in the Fire.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage addresses the fate of children of polytheists who die before maturity. It presents three positions: (1) The majority opinion holds they are in Hell, based on general scriptural texts and the hadith about Khadija's children. (2) The Mu'tazila and their followers hold they are not punished but serve as servants of Paradise, citing the injustice of punishing the innocent and verses against bearing others' burdens. (3) A third opinion ties their fate to divine foreknowledge: if God knows they would have believed at maturity, they are in Paradise; if He knows they would have disbelieved, they are in Hell. The passage does not endorse any position but presents the views.

Key Terms
الكفار حكماً
أطفال المشركين
خدم أهل الجنة
تقدير البلوغ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All children of disbelievers automatically go to Paradise.
Correction: The majority opinion holds that children of polytheists are in Hell, based on a hadith and general texts. The Mu'tazila disagree, but the third view depends on divine foreknowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila, what happens to children of polytheists who die before maturity?
A) They are punished in Hell.
B) They become servants of the people of Paradise and are not punished.
C) They go to a middle state between Paradise and Hell.
D) They are reincarnated.

Key Takeaway
The fate of children of polytheists who die before maturity is disputed among Islamic scholars, with three main opinions based on different interpretations of divine justice and foreknowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that the Prophet ﷺ told Khadīja that her children who died in pre-Islamic times are in the Fire, how does this shape your understanding of the gravity of disbelief and the urgency of calling your family to the truth? What specific steps will you take this week to share Islam with a loved one who is not practicing?
?
The Mu'tazila argued that punishing the innocent is unjust. Reflect on your own life: are there times you justify harshness towards others by claiming they 'deserve' it, forgetting that true justice belongs only to Allah? How can you embody mercy in a judgment today?
?
The third opinion ties salvation to what Allah knows you would have done. Are you living today as if your fate is already written, or are you actively striving to fulfill your potential as a believer? What one habit must you change to align your actions with your faith?

The Ash'ari Position on Major Sinners
Presents the Ash'ari view on major sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position on the fate of a believer who dies unrepentant from a major sin, particularly that both forgiveness and punishment are possible but eventual exit from Hell is guaranteed by God's promise.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari view: neither forgiveness nor punishment is certain, but eventual exit from Hell is promised.

The passage opens with the differing opinions among Muslims on the fate of major sinners. The Ash'ari position is presented first: a middle path between definitive forgiveness and definitive eternal punishment. This lesson unpacks that nuanced stance, explaining the role of God's will and the promise (wa'd) that ensures eventual salvation for believers who enter Hell.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Begin by reading the Arabic text carefully. Notice the key terms: الكبيرة, الوعيد, الخروج من النار.
The passage starts with a general statement about disagreement, then gives the Ash'ari view.
2
Identify the core thesis
The Ash'ari position is that neither forgiveness nor punishment is definitively affirmed; both are subject to God's will. However, if punishment is decreed, the sinner will eventually leave Hell.
This is not based on obligation on God, but on His previous promise (wa'd) established by evidence.
3
Understand the logic behind eventual exit
The author compares it to the eternal abiding of the people of Paradise—both are based on God's promise, not on any necessity on God's part.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف أهل الإسلام فيمن ارتكب الكبيرة من المؤمنين ومات قبل التوبة ، فالمذهب عندنا عدم القطع بالعفو ولا بالعقاب بل كلاهما في مشيئة الله تعالى لكن على تقدير التعذيب نقطع بأنه لا يخلد في النار، بل يخرج البتة، لا بطريق الوجوب على الله تعالى، بل بمقتضى ما سبق من الوعد . وثبت بالدليل كتخليد أهل الجنة . وعند المعتزلة القطع بالعذاب الدائم من غير عفو ولا إخراج من النار، ويعبر عن هذا بمسألة وعيد الفساق، وعقوبة العصاة، وانقطاع عذاب أهل الكبائر، ونحو ذلك (۳). وليس في مسألة الاستحقاق ووجوب العقاب غنى عن ذلك، لأن التخليد أمر زائد على التعذيب. ولا في مسألة العفو، لأنه بطريق الاحتمال دون القطع ، ولأنه شاع في ترك العقاب بالكلية، وهذا قطع بالخروج بعد الدخول، وما وقع في كلام البعض من أن صاحب الكبيرة عند المعتزلة ليس في الجنة ولا في النار فغلط نشأ من قولهم : إن له المنزلة بين المنزلتين. أي حالة غير الإيمان والكفر . وأما ما ذهب إليه مقاتل بن سليمان وبعض المرجئة من أن عصاة المؤمنين لا يعذبون أصلاً، وإنما النار للكفار تمسكاً بالآيات الدالة على اختصاص العذاب بالكفار مثل :
And the people of Islam differed concerning one who commits a major sin (kabira) among the believers and dies before repentance. The madhhab with us is to not affirm forgiveness definitively nor punishment definitively; rather both are in the will of Allah Almighty. But on the assumption of punishment, we affirm that he will not eternally remain in the Fire; rather he will surely exit, not by way of obligation upon Allah Almighty, but by virtue of the previous promise (wa'd). And it is established by evidence like the eternal abiding of the people of Paradise. With the Mu'tazila, there is definitive assertion of perpetual punishment without forgiveness or exit from the Fire, and this is expressed as the issue of the threat (wa'id) against the wicked, the punishment of the disobedient, and the cessation of the punishment of the people of major sins, and similar expressions (3). And there is no need for the issue of desert (istihqaq) and obligation of punishment regarding that, because eternal abiding (takhld) is additional to punishment. Nor regarding the issue of forgiveness, because it is by way of possibility (ihtimal) rather than definitiveness, and because it has become widespread in the sense of complete remission of punishment; whereas this is a definitive exit after entry. And what has occurred in the speech of some, that the committer of a major sin according to the Mu'tazila is neither in Paradise nor in Hell, is an error arising from their saying: he has the station between the two stations (al-manzila bayn al-manzilatayn), i.e. a state other than faith and disbelief. As for what was held by Muqatil ibn Sulayman and some of the Murji'a, that disobedient believers are not punished at all, and that the Fire is only for the disbelievers, clinging to verses indicating the restriction of punishment to the disbelievers, such as:
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents three positions on believers who die without repenting from major sins. (1) The Ash'ari position: neither forgiveness nor punishment is affirmed definitively; both are subject to God's will. However, if punishment is decreed, the person will eventually exit Hell—not because God is obligated, but due to His promise (wa'd) established by evidence like the eternity of Paradise. (2) The Mu'tazili position: perpetual punishment without forgiveness or exit, called the 'issue of wa'id against the wicked.' The author notes that the famous phrase 'station between the two stations' is often misunderstood: it refers to a state between faith and disbelief in this world, not a physical location. (3) The Murji'ite position attributed to Muqatil ibn Sulayman: no punishment at all for disobedient believers; only disbelievers enter Hell. The passage ends with a reference to verses claiming punishment is exclusive to disbelievers.

Key Terms
الكبيرة
الوعيد
الخروج من النار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ash'aris believe all major sinners are definitely forgiven and never face punishment.
Correction: Ash'aris hold that punishment is possible (if God wills), but eventual exit is certain due to God's promise, not that there is no punishment.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari position, what is the fate of a believer who dies unrepentant from a major sin?
A) He is definitely forgiven.
B) He is definitely punished eternally.
C) Forgiveness and punishment are both possible; if punished, he will eventually leave Hell.
D) He remains in a state between Paradise and Hell.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari position balances God's will and His promise: major sinners may be punished but not eternally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight after committing a major sin without having repented, are you truly comfortable leaving your fate entirely in God's will? How does that realization challenge your current attitude toward repentance?
?
The Ash'aris believe God's promise of eventual exit is not out of obligation but pure mercy. Do you live with a hope that is based on God's promise, or do you secretly rely on your own deeds? What needs to change today?
?
This passage says both forgiveness and punishment are possible but not certain. Does that uncertainty make you more fearful of falling into sin or more hopeful of God's mercy? And what does your answer reveal about your trust in God's character?

The Mu'tazili Position and Clarification of 'al-Manzi...'
Presents Mu'tazili view and corrects misinterpretation of their concept.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili view that major sinners face perpetual punishment and the correct meaning of their phrase 'al-manzila bayn al-manzilatayn' as a worldly state, not a physical location.

Core Idea
Mu'tazilis hold that major sinners are punished eternally; their 'station between stations' is a worldly state, not a place.

This lesson covers the Mu'tazili position on major sinners, which contrasts sharply with the Ash'ari view. Additionally, the passage corrects a common misinterpretation of the Mu'tazili concept of 'al-manzila bayn al-manzilatayn', explaining it refers to a state in this world, not a literal location between Paradise and Hell.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazili position
The Mu'tazila definitively assert perpetual punishment without forgiveness or exit. This is called the issue of wa'id (threat).
Note the difference from Ash'aris: Mu'tazilis hold that punishment is certain and eternal.
2
Understand the author's critique
The author argues that the concepts of desert (istihqaq) and obligation are not relevant here because eternal abiding is additional to punishment, and forgiveness is not the same as exit after entry.
3
Correct the misunderstanding
The phrase 'al-manzila bayn al-manzilatayn' is often misunderstood as a physical place. The author clarifies it means a state in this world between faith and disbelief.
This is a key clarification.

The Murji'i Position: No Punishment for Believing Sinners
Presents the Murji'i view of no punishment for believing sinners.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Some Murji'ites hold that no believing sinner will ever enter Hell; punishment is only for disbelievers.

The final position presented is that of Muqatil ibn Sulayman and some Murji'ites, who assert that believers who commit sins will not be punished at all, arguing from verses that seem to limit punishment to the disbelievers. The passage ends with a reference to such verses, but the full argument is cut off.

2

The full argument is not given in this excerpt.
3

Note how this view differs: Ash'aris allow for punishment with eventual exit, Mu'tazilis affirm eternal punishment, while Murji'ites deny any punishment for believers.

The Fate of Children of Polytheists: Hadith vs. Mu'tazila View
Reports the hadith and Mu'tazila view on children of polytheists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conflicting views on the fate of children of polytheists who died before Islam, specifically the hadith report and the Mu'tazila interpretation.

Core Idea
The fate of innocent children divides Sunni orthodoxy and Mu'tazila rationalism.

This passage presents a pointed disagreement between a direct prophetic statement and a rational theological principle. The Prophet told Khadija that her children who died in the pre-Islamic period are in the Fire, yet the Mu'tazila argued that punishing those without sin contradicts divine justice. This lesson examines the conflicting evidence and the theological stakes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Note the direct statement from the Prophet and the Mu'tazila response.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage contains two distinct positions: the Prophet's statement that the children are in the Fire, and the Mu'tazila view that they are not punished but are servants of Paradise.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila proof
The Mu'tazila support their view with a hadith and the rational principle that punishing the innocent is unjust, citing Quranic verses on personal responsibility.
This shows that the Mu'tazila also appeal to scripture, not just reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خديجة (رضي الله عنها) سألت النبي عليه السلام عن أطفالها الذين ماتوا في الجاهلية، فقال : هم في النار. وقالت المعتزلة، ومن تبعهم : لا يعذبون بل هم خدم أهل الجنة ، على ما ورد الحديث، لأن تعذيب من لا جرم له ظلم ولقوله: ﴿ ولا تزر وازرة وزر أخرى ﴾ ولا تجزون إلا ما كنتم تعملون. ونحو ذلك .
Khadija (may Allah be pleased with her) asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about her children who died in the pre-Islamic period. He said: 'They are in the Fire.' The Mu'tazila and those who follow them said: 'They are not punished, rather they are servants of the people of Paradise, according to the hadith that has come, because punishing one who has no sin is injustice, and due to His statement: 'And no bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another' (Quran 6:164, 35:18) and 'You will not be recompensed except for what you used to do' (Quran 36:54). And similar [statements].
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage reports a specific incident and then contrasts it with the Mu'tazila view. The author first narrates that Khadija asked the Prophet about her children who died before Islam. The Prophet replied that they are in the Fire. This is a direct hadith on the matter. Then the author mentions that the Mu'tazila and their followers hold a different opinion: they say those children are not punished but are servants of the people of Paradise, citing a hadith and the principle that punishing the innocent is unjust, and the Quranic verses that emphasize personal responsibility. The passage thus sets up a key point of disagreement, which leads into the broader discussion of the fate of sinners.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الجاهلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila view is based solely on rational argument without scriptural support.
Correction: The passage shows they also cite a hadith and Quranic verses, not just reason.

Checkpoint
What was the Prophet's response to Khadija's question about her children who died in the pre-Islamic period?
A) They are in Paradise.
B) They are in the Fire.
C) They are not punished.
D) They are servants of the people of Paradise.

Key Takeaway
The fate of children of polytheists is disputed between a literal hadith and a rational-ethical principle, highlighting tensions in theological methodology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a clear hadith from the Prophet that conflicts with a principle of justice you hold dear, which do you trust? Are you willing to accept a truth that seems unfair to your own sense of justice, or will you rationalize it away?
?
The Mu'tazila used their reasoning to soften the fate of innocent children. Does your heart lean towards their view because it seems more merciful? How do you reconcile that with the words of the Prophet? What does this reveal about the role of your emotions in accepting religious truths?
?
If you were in Khadija's place, hearing that your own children are in the Fire, how would you respond? Would you question the Prophet's judgment or submit? What does that tell you about your own tawakkul (reliance on Allah) and your willingness to accept divine decree even when it is painful?

Refuting the view that sinful believers face no punishment
Refutation of Muqatil and Murji'a on punishment of sinful believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutation of Muqatil and the Murji'a claim that believing sinners are not punished at all.

Core Idea
Even sinful believers may face temporary punishment, contrary to Murji'a extreme optimism.

This lesson addresses an extreme position within early Islamic theology that denied any punishment for sinful believers. Muqatil ibn Sulayman and some Murji'a argued that only disbelievers face the Fire. By examining the Quranic verses and hadith they relied on, we see how the scholars clarified that punishment for believers is not eternal but not entirely absent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument unfold.
The passage is short but dense. Note the two proofs of the opposing view.
2
Identify the two arguments of Muqatil and the Murji'a
Find the Quranic verses they cited (20:48 and 16:27) and the hadith about 'man qala la ilaha illa Allah.' Understand how they used these as evidence.
The hadith is well-known; focus on how it was interpreted by this group.
3
Understand the refutation of the Quranic proof
The author responds that the verses are about a punishment that is not eternal. That means they do not negate temporary punishment for believers.
This is a key point: the verses are general but not absolute regarding eternity.
4
Understand the refutation of the hadith proof
The author points out that the hadith only negates eternal punishment (khulud), not entry into the Fire for a time. The hadith is also considered weak (da'if) for this argument.
The refutation is that the hadith does not support their claim that believers are not punished at all.
5
Summarise the lesson
Restate the main points: Muqatil's claim, their evidence, and the two refutations. Check your understanding with the checkpoint.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما ذهب إليه مقاتل بن سليمان وبعض المرجئة من أن عصاة المؤمنين لا يعذبون أصلاً، وإنما النار للكفار تمسكاً بالآيات الدالة على اختصاص العذاب بالكفار مثل : (إنا قد أوحي إلينا أن العذاب على من كذب وتولى) (إن الخزى اليوم والسوء على الكافرين) فجوابه تخصيص ذلك بعذاب لا يكون على سبيل الخلود، وأما تمسكهم بمثل قوله (عليه السلام) من قال : لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة وإن زنى وإن سرق» فضعيف لأنه إنما ينفي الخلود لا الدخول
And as for what Muqatil ibn Sulayman and some of the Murji'a held, that the disobedient believers are not punished at all, and that the Fire is only for the disbelievers, clinging to the verses that indicate the restriction of punishment to the disbelievers, such as: 'It has been revealed to us that the punishment is upon whoever denies and turns away' (Quran 20:48) and 'Indeed, disgrace today and evil are upon the disbelievers' (Quran 16:27). The response to it is that this is specified to a punishment that is not of the sort of eternity. And as for their clinging to such sayings as his (peace be upon him) 'Whoever says there is no god but Allah will enter Paradise, even if he fornicates and steals,' it is weak because it only negates eternity, not entry [into the Fire].
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an extreme view held by Muqatil ibn Sulayman and some Murji'a. They argued that believing sinners are not punished at all; only disbelievers enter the Fire. They cited Quranic verses that appear to limit punishment to disbelievers, such as 'the punishment is upon whoever denies and turns away' and 'disgrace and evil are upon the disbelievers.' The author responds by saying that these verses apply to a punishment that is not eternal (i.e., temporary punishment for believers is not excluded, only eternal punishment is for disbelievers). The second argument of this group is based on the hadith 'Whoever says there is no god but Allah will enter Paradise, even if he fornicates and steals.' The author points out that this hadith is weak (da'if) as evidence here because it only negates eternal punishment, not entry into the Fire for a time. Thus, the refutation clarifies that the Quranic verses about punishment for disbelievers do not preclude temporary punishment for sinful believers, and the hadith cited does not support their claim when properly understood.

Key Terms
مقاتل بن سليمان
المرجئة
الخلود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'Whoever says there is no god but Allah will enter Paradise, even if he fornicates and steals' guarantees immediate Paradise without any punishment.
Correction: The hadith only negates eternal punishment, not entry into the Fire for a period of time.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument of Muqatil and the Murji'a that the author refutes?
A) That believers who sin will be punished eternally.
B) That believers who sin are not punished at all.
C) That believers who sin will have a station between Paradise and Hell.
D) That the Fire is for both believers and disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
Quranic verses about punishment for disbelievers do not preclude temporary punishment for sinful believers, and the hadith only negates eternity, not entry into the Fire.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever reassured yourself that a sin you committed is 'not that bad' because you believe in Allah? How does this lesson's refutation of the Murji'a position challenge that kind of complacency, and what concrete step will you take to take sin more seriously?
?
The hadith 'Whoever says la ilaha illa Allah will enter Paradise' is often used to comfort people. After learning its correct meaning (negating eternity, not entry into Fire), how does this change the way you would counsel a friend who is indulging in sin while relying on this hadith?
?
When you read Quranic verses that threaten punishment exclusively on disbelievers, were you tempted to think they don't apply to you? How does the distinction between eternal and temporary punishment force you to re-evaluate your own accountability, and what will you do differently today?

First Proof: Believers Enter Paradise
First proof for non-eternity of punishment using Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof for the non-eternity of punishment for grave sinners, based on Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths that guarantee believers' entry into Paradise.

Core Idea
Believers will definitely enter Paradise, so punishment must end or be forgiven.

This lesson introduces the primary proof used by Ash'ari theologians to argue that grave sinners among the believers will not remain in Hell forever. The reasoning relies on clear scriptural texts that promise Paradise to believers, which logically forces one of two outcomes: either they leave the Fire after a period of punishment (termination), or they are forgiven entirely and never enter it. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice the author begins with 'lana wujuh' (we have proofs) and then presents the first proof as the main one (al-`umda).
The passage is concise; each scriptural citation supports the guarantee of Paradise for believers.
2
Identify the two possibilities
After stating that believers will definitely enter Paradise, the author says that this entry must occur either after entering the Fire (meaning punishment ends) or without entering the Fire (complete forgiveness). Identify these two possibilities in the text.
Look for phrases 'inqita' al-'adhab' and 'al-'afw al-tamm'.
3
Examine the Quranic verses
The author cites two Quranic verses: Surah al-Zalzala (99:7-8) and Surah al-Nisa (4:124). Reflect on how these verses indicate that believers will see good and enter Paradise, implying eventual reward.
4
Examine the hadiths
Two hadiths are quoted: 'Whoever says la ilaha illa Allah enters Paradise' and 'Whoever dies not associating anything with Allah enters Paradise, even if he fornicates and steals.' Note how these hadiths explicitly guarantee Paradise for believers, even those who commit major sins.
This counters the Mu'tazilite view that grave sinners are eternally punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لنا وجوه :
الأول - وهو العمدة، الآيات والأحاديث الدالة على أن المؤمنين يدخلون الجنة البتة، وليس ذلك قبل دخول النار وفاقاً، فتعين أن يكون بعده ، وهو مسألة انقطاع العذاب، أو بدونه وهو مسألة العفو التام. قال الله تعالى : فمن يعمل مثقال ذرة خيراً يره ومن يعمل صالحاً من ذكر أو أنثى وهو مؤمن فأولئك يدخلون الجنة . وقال النبي عليه السلام : من قال: لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة». وقال: مات لا يشرك بالله شيئاً دخل الجنة، وإن زنى وإن سرق». من
We have proofs:
First - and it is the main one: the verses and hadiths that indicate that the believers will definitely enter Paradise, and that is not before entering the Fire by agreement, so it must be after it, and that is the issue of the termination of punishment (inqita' al-'adhab), or without it, and that is the issue of complete forgiveness (al-'afw al-tamm). Allah Most High said: 'So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it' (Quran 99:7-8) and 'Whoever does righteousness, whether male or female, while he is a believer - those will enter Paradise' (Quran 4:124). And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever says there is no god but Allah will enter Paradise.' And he said: 'He who dies not associating anything with Allah will enter Paradise, even if he fornicates and steals.' ... min
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage begins enumeration of proofs. The author states that we (Ash'aris) have several proofs. The first and most important (al-`umda) is based on verses and hadiths that definitively indicate that believers will enter Paradise. It is agreed that this entry does not occur before entering the Fire (i.e., believers do not go directly to Paradise without any prior punishment if they have sins). Therefore, it must be after entering the Fire, which is the issue of 'termination of punishment' (that punishment ends and the person is removed), or without entering the Fire at all, which is the issue of 'complete forgiveness' (that Allah forgives the sin and the person goes straight to Paradise). The author then cites two Quranic verses: 'Whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it' (99:7-8) and 'Whoever does righteousness, male or female, while a believer – those will enter Paradise' (4:124). These imply that believers will eventually see the reward and enter Paradise, after any possible punishment. Then two hadiths are cited: 'Whoever says there is no god but Allah will enter Paradise' and 'He who dies not associating anything with Allah will enter Paradise, even if he fornicates and steals.' These hadiths also assure entry into Paradise, which logically either occurs after release from Fire or without any Fire. Thus this proof establishes that a sinful believer will not be eternally in Hell.

Key Terms
العمدة
انقطاع العذاب
العفو التام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'Whoever says la ilaha illa Allah will enter Paradise' is understood by some to mean immediate entry without any accountability or punishment.
Correction: The text clarifies that this entry occurs after possible punishment, not before, as it says 'not before entering the Fire by agreement.' The hadith guarantees eventual entry, not immediate.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what does the certainty that believers will enter Paradise imply?
A) They will never enter the Fire.
B) They must either leave the Fire after entry or be forgiven entirely.
C) They will be punished eternally.
D) They will have a station between Paradise and Hell.

Key Takeaway
The scriptural promise that believers will enter Paradise logically requires that punishment for grave sinners either ends (they leave the Fire) or is completely forgiven (they never enter it).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die right now, do you honestly believe you have the sincere faith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) promised would lead to Paradise? What sins are you holding onto that make you doubt this promise?
?
The hadith says even a fornicator and thief will enter Paradise if they die not associating anything with Allah. Does this give you false comfort to continue sinning, or does it deepen your gratitude for Allah's mercy? What will you change today to ensure your faith remains pure?
?
The proof concludes that punishment must end or be forgiven. How does this affect your view of your own sins? Are you relying on the end of punishment or on Allah's complete forgiveness? What steps can you take to seek the latter?

Second Proof: Texts Indicating Exit from Fire
The author presents the second proof from texts indicating exit from Fire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses Quranic verses and a hadith to argue for the eventual removal of sinful believers from Hell, and why the solitary report is considered supportive.

Core Idea
Even weak texts, when combined, can support the possibility of leaving the Fire.

In this lesson, we examine the second proof from the author, which relies on explicit scriptural texts that hint at the possibility of leaving Hell. The author cites two Quranic verses and a hadith, and then explains how these texts, even if individually not decisive, together provide strong support.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the full meaning.
Notice the exception clause in the first verse.
2
Identify the texts used
List the Quranic verses and the hadith. Consider what each one explicitly says about exiting the Fire.
These are the building blocks of the proof.
3
Understand the role of khabar al-wahid
The author notes that solitary reports are not decisive in fundamentals, but they provide support when combined. Reflect on why this matters for the argument.
This addresses a potential objection about weak hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - النصوص المشعرة بالخروج من النار كقوله تعالى : النار مثواكم خالدين فيها إلا ما شاء الله فمن زحزح عن النار وأدخل الجنة فقد فاز وكقوله (عليه السلام) يخرج من النار قوم بعدما امتحشوا وصاروا فحماً وحمماً، فينبتون كما تنبت الحبة في حميل السيل . وخبر الواحد، وإن لم يكن حجة في الأصول، لكن يفيد التأييد والتأكيد بتعاضد النصوص.
Second: the texts that indicate exit from the Fire, such as His statement (Most High): 'The Fire will be your abode, eternally abiding therein, except as Allah wills' (Quran 6:128) and 'Whoever is removed from the Fire and admitted to Paradise has certainly attained success' (Quran 3:185). And his statement (peace be upon him): 'People will come out of the Fire after they have been charred and become charcoal and embers; then they will grow as a seed grows in the silt of a flood.' And the solitary report (khabar al-wahid), even if it is not a proof in the fundamentals (usul), still provides support and reinforcement due to the mutual strengthening of the texts.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for the Ash'ari position that sinful believers will not be eternally punished and will eventually be removed from Hell. The proof relies on textual evidence (nusus) that explicitly indicates exit from the Fire. The author cites two Quranic verses: first, 'The Fire will be your abode, eternally abiding therein, except as Allah wills' (6:128). The exception 'except as Allah wills' leaves open the possibility that some may be released. Second, 'Whoever is removed from the Fire and admitted to Paradise has certainly attained success' (3:185) – this implies there is such a thing as being removed from the Fire. Then a hadith is cited: 'People will come out of the Fire after they have been charred and become charcoal and embers, then they will grow as a seed grows in the silt of a flood.' This hadith is a solitary report (khabar al-wahid). The author notes that while a solitary report is not considered a decisive proof in theological fundamentals (usul al-din), it does provide support (ta'yid) and reinforcement (ta'kid) when combined with other texts. Thus, the cumulative evidence supports the conclusion that believers will be removed from the Fire.

Key Terms
النصوص المشعرة
خبر الواحد
الأصول
التأييد
التأكيد
تعاضد النصوص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That khabar al-wahid is never used in theology and is completely ignored.
Correction: The author explains that although it is not a decisive proof in fundamentals, it still provides support and reinforcement when combined with other texts.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what status does the hadith about people coming out of the Fire have in theological proof?
A) It is a decisive proof (hujja) in the fundamentals.
B) It is weak and cannot be used at all.
C) It provides support and reinforcement due to mutual strengthening.
D) It indicates that no one will be removed from the Fire.

Key Takeaway
The second proof uses scriptural texts that imply exit from the Fire, and the solitary report, though not foundational, reinforces this conclusion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof relies on the exception 'except as Allah wills'. Do you truly believe that Allah's mercy can override the punishment you deserve, or do you secretly assume you will be fine without any effort? What change in your daily actions would reflect genuine hope in this mercy?
?
The solitary report only provides support, not decisive proof. Are you willing to live your life on a 'supported' hope, or do you demand absolute certainty before you let a text affect your heart? How does that affect your relationship with weaker hadith?
?
The hadith describes people leaving the Fire like seeds growing from silt. Picture yourself as one of those charred remnants. Does that image provoke more gratitude for Allah's mercy or more complacency in sin? Honestly, which of these feelings dominates, and what will you do about it?

Refuting Objections on Eternal Punishment
Refutes opponent's use of verses and a hadith to prove eternal punishment for sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes scriptural evidence used to support eternal punishment for all sinners by distinguishing between temporary and eternal punishment.

Core Idea
Scriptural threats of punishment do not automatically imply eternity.

This passage addresses two key objections raised by opponents who use Quranic verses and a prophetic hadith to argue that sinners face eternal punishment. The author provides concise responses that clarify that the verses refer to non-eternal punishment and that the hadith only guarantees eventual entry into paradise, not immediate entry without prior punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: two objections followed by responses.
The Arabic includes Quranic phrases in parentheses.
2
Identify the two objections
First objection: Quranic verses threatening punishment for deniers. Second objection: Hadith about entering paradise through the declaration of faith.
The opponents use these to claim all sinners face eternal punishment.
3
Understand the author's responses
For the verses, the author says they specify a punishment that is not eternal. For the hadith, he says it only negates eternal punishment, not entry after temporary punishment.
The key terms are al-khulud (eternity) and al-dukhul (entry).
4
Connect to the broader doctrine
This refutation supports the Ash'ari position that grave sinners may be temporarily punished before entering paradise, as opposed to eternal damnation.
This is a central point in Islamic theology about the fate of sinful believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنا قد أوحي إلينا أن العذاب على من كذب وتولى) إن الخزى اليوم والسوء على الكافرين ) فجوابه تخصيص ذلك بعذاب لا يكون على سبيل الخلود، وأما تمسكهم بمثل قوله (عليه السلام) من قال : لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة وإن زنى وإن سرق» فضعيف لأنه إنما ينفي الخلود لا الدخول
We have indeed been inspired that the punishment is upon those who deny and turn away. 'Disgrace today and evil upon the disbelievers.' So the answer is to specify that as a punishment that is not eternal. As for their holding fast to something like his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever says: There is no god but Allah enters paradise, even if he fornicates and steals,' it is weak because it only negates eternity, not entry.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage begins by presenting two objections from opponents and the author's responses. First, the opponents cite Quranic verses that threaten punishment for those who deny and disbelieve (Surah TaHa 48 and Surah An-Nahl 27) to argue that sinners face eternal punishment. The author answers that these verses are specific to a punishment that is not eternal (i.e., exclusive to disbelievers or temporary). Second, the opponents cite the hadith that whoever says 'La ilaha illallah' enters paradise even if he fornicates and steals, arguing that this proves no punishment at all. The author responds that this hadith is weak or misunderstood: it only negates eternal punishment (khulud), not temporary punishment before entry into paradise. Thus, the hadith does not conflict with temporary punishment for grave sins.

Key Terms
الخلود
الدخول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the hadith 'man qala la ilaha illallah dakhala al-janna' means immediate entry into paradise without any prior punishment, thus ruling out temporary punishment for grave sinners.
Correction: The author clarifies that the hadith only negates eternal punishment (khulud), not entry after temporary punishment. A person may still be punished temporarily in Hell before entering Paradise.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the hadith 'Whoever says la ilaha illallah enters paradise, even if he fornicates and steals' not a valid proof against temporary punishment?
A) It is a weak hadith.
B) It only negates eternal punishment, not entry into paradise after punishment.
C) It applies only to disbelievers.
D) It was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The author demonstrates that scriptural proofs can be interpreted to allow temporary punishment, as they do not necessitate eternity of punishment for sinners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a major sin, do you assume that because you believe in Allah you will avoid any punishment? How does this lesson's distinction between eternal and temporary punishment challenge that assumption?
?
The hadith promises Paradise even for fornicators and thieves. Does this make you less fearful of sinning, or does it increase your hope in Allah's mercy while motivating you to avoid temporary punishment? Answer honestly.
?
If you knew that a temporary punishment in Hell awaits you for your sins, what would you change in your life today? Write one concrete action you will take to avoid that punishment.

First proof: Every believer enters paradise
First proof from Quran and hadith for eventual paradise of believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first and main proof from Quran and hadith that all believers will eventually enter paradise, either after punishment or by complete pardon.

Core Idea
Every believer is guaranteed paradise, even if after punishment.

This lesson presents the foundational proof from scripture that no believer will be forever damned. The author establishes that paradise is assured for every believer, but not necessarily before some purifying punishment. The Quranic verses and hadith cited here form the bedrock of the Ash'ari position on the fate of sinful believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the logical structure: first the claim, then the deduction, then the scriptural evidence.
The passage is concise; every sentence builds the argument.
2
Identify the three components
Identify the claim (believers enter paradise absolutely), the logical deduction (it must be after or without punishment), and the evidence (two Quranic verses and two hadith).
3
Understand the logical progression
Since it is agreed that entry is not before entering the fire, it must be either after punishment (cessation) or without punishment (complete pardon). This logic is key.
The phrase 'البتة' emphasizes certainty.
4
Reflect on implications
Consider how this proof upholds both divine justice (punishment for sins) and mercy (eventual paradise for all believers).
This balances fear and hope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لنا وجوه : الأول - وهو العمدة، الآيات والأحاديث الدالة على أن المؤمنين يدخلون الجنة البتة، وليس ذلك قبل دخول النار وفاقاً، فتعين أن يكون بعده ، وهو مسألة انقطاع العذاب، أو بدونه وهو مسألة العفو التام. قال الله تعالى : فمن يعمل مثقال ذرة خيراً يره (۳) وومن يعمل صالحاً من ذكر أو أنثى وهو مؤمن فأولئك يدخلون الجنة (٤) . وقال النبي عليه السلام : من قال: لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة». وقال: مات لا يشرك بالله شيئاً دخل الجنة، وإن زنى وإن سرق».
We have proofs: First—and it is the main one—the verses and hadith that indicate that believers enter paradise absolutely, and that is not before entering the fire by agreement, so it must be after it—which is the issue of the cessation of punishment—or without it—which is the issue of complete pardon. Allah Most High said: 'So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it' (Surah al-Zalzalah 7-8) and 'Whoever does righteousness, male or female, while being a believer—those will enter paradise' (Surah al-Nisa 124). And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever says: There is no god but Allah enters paradise.' And he said: 'Whoever dies not associating anything with Allah enters paradise, even if he fornicates and steals.'
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage presents the first and most important proof (العمدة) for the Ash'ari position that sinful believers will eventually enter paradise. The author states that Quranic verses and prophetic hadith definitively (البتة) indicate that all believers enter paradise. It is agreed (وفاقاً) that this entry does not occur before entering the fire—meaning that sinners do not go directly to paradise without any punishment. Therefore, entry must be after punishment (the issue of cessation of punishment, انقطاع العذاب) or without punishment but after some other state (the issue of complete pardon, العفو التام). The author then cites two Quranic verses: 'Whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it' (Surah al-Zalzalah 7-8) and 'Whoever does righteousness... while being a believer—those will enter paradise' (Surah al-Nisa 124) to support that good deeds and faith guarantee eventual paradise. Two hadith are also cited: one that simply states 'whoever says la ilaha illallah enters paradise,' and another that adds 'even if he fornicates and steals,' reinforcing that even grave sins do not prevent final entry, though they may entail temporary punishment.

Key Terms
البتة
انقطاع العذاب
العفو التام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'dakhala al-janna' means immediate entry into paradise without any prior punishment.
Correction: The author clarifies that entry is absolute but not before entering the fire; it can be after punishment or by complete pardon.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what is the agreed-upon fact about the entry of believers into paradise?
A) They enter paradise before the fire.
B) They enter paradise after the fire.
C) They do not enter paradise at all if they sinned.
D) They enter paradise only if they never committed a grave sin.

Key Takeaway
The first and strongest proof for the Ash'ari position is that scripture guarantees paradise for all believers, either after punishment or by divine pardon.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If paradise is guaranteed for every believer, does that make you less worried about your sins? Or does it make you more eager to avoid punishment by seeking pardon?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing major sins, do you despair of their final outcome? How should this hadith change your attitude?
?
Are you living as though entering paradise is certain enough that you neglect repentance? Or are you striving to minimize punishment by seeking complete pardon?

Second Proof: Scriptural Indications of Removal from Hell
Cites Quran and hadith to argue for removal from hell with methodological note

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses Quranic verses and a hadith to argue for the possibility of removal from hell, and how solitary reports gain credibility through corroboration.

Core Idea
Even a solitary hadith can support a doctrinal point when many texts reinforce each other.

In this passage, the author presents the second proof: scriptural texts that explicitly indicate that some people may leave hell after purification. He cites two Quranic verses and a hadith, then addresses the common objection that the hadith is only a solitary report. This lesson will walk you through the evidence and the methodological principle of corroboration.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and notice the sources used
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the two Quranic verses and the hadith.
The verses are from Surah al-An'am and Surah Al 'Imran.
2
Understand the 'except as Allah wills' clause
Reflect on how the phrase 'except as Allah wills' in Quran 6:128 opens the door for exceptions to eternal punishment.
This is a key textual basis for the doctrine.
3
Analyze the hadith about coming out of hell
The hadith describes people who become like charcoal then sprout. Consider how this supports the idea of removal after purification.
4
Examine the methodological point about khabar al-wahid
The author admits that solitary reports are not authoritative in fundamentals, but argues that corroboration from multiple texts provides strong support.
This shows the author's balanced approach to hadith evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - النصوص المشعرة بالخروج من النار كقوله تعالى : النار مثواكم خالدين فيها إلا ما شاء الله (٥) فمن زحزح عن النار وأدخل الجنة فقد فاز (٦) وكقوله (عليه السلام) يخرج من النار قوم بعدما امتحشوا وصاروا فحماً وحمماً، فينبتون كما تنبت الحبة في حميل السيل». وخبر الواحد، وإن لم يكن حجة في الأصول، لكن يفيد التأييد والتأكيد بتعاضد النصوص.
Second—the texts that indicate exit from the fire, such as His Most High's saying: 'The fire is your abode, abiding therein, except as Allah wills' (Surah al-An'am 128) and 'Whoever is removed from the fire and entered into paradise has succeeded' (Surah Al 'Imran 185), and like his saying (peace be upon him): 'People will come out of the fire after they have been scorched and become charcoal and cinders, then they will sprout as the seed sprouts in the silt of a torrent.' And the solitary report, though not authoritative in fundamental matters, yet provides support and emphasis through the corroboration of texts.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof: scriptural texts that directly indicate the possibility of leaving hell. The author cites Quran 6:128 which says 'except as Allah wills'—implying that eternity in hell may have exceptions. He also cites Quran 3:185: 'Whoever is removed from the fire and entered into paradise has succeeded,' which explicitly mentions removal from the fire. Then a hadith describes people coming out of hell after being burned into charcoal, then sprouting like seeds. The author addresses a methodological point: the hadith quoted is a solitary report (خبر الواحد), which by itself is not authoritative as proof in fundamental creedal matters (الأصول). However, because many such texts corroborate each other (بتعاضد النصوص), they collectively provide strong support (التأييد والتأكيد) for the doctrine.

Key Terms
النصوص المشعرة بالخروج
خبر الواحد
تعاضد النصوص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid) cannot be used as any form of evidence in creedal matters.
Correction: The author states that while it is not a definitive proof in fundamentals, it does provide support and emphasis when corroborated by other texts.

Checkpoint
How does the author justify using a solitary hadith for removal from hell?
A) It is explicitly confirmed by consensus.
B) It is corroborated by many other texts, providing reinforcement.
C) It is a mutawatir hadith.
D) It is rationally necessary.

Key Takeaway
Scriptural texts, when taken together, strongly suggest that believers may be removed from hell after purification, even if individual reports are not independently authoritative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a prophetic hadith because you thought it was 'too weak' to affect your beliefs? This lesson shows that even a solitary report, when corroborated, can carry weight. Will you now reconsider how you treat hadith that challenge your comfortable assumptions about hell?
?
The fire is described as an 'abode' except as Allah wills. Does this exception fill you with hope or fear? What does your actual daily life say about your reliance on Allah's mercy versus your own deeds? Today, pause and ask yourself: Am I living as if I expect to be purified by fire, or as if I hope to avoid it entirely?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) described people coming out of hell like seeds sprouting from silt. Do you truly believe that Allah's mercy can transform even a person reduced to 'charcoal and cinders'? If so, what does that mean for how you view yourself—and how you view others who have fallen into sin? What one step will you take today to be among those who are removed?

Third Proof: Justice Argument from Mu'tazilite Principle
Uses Mu'tazilite principle to argue against eternal punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses the Mu'tazilite's own concept of divine justice to argue that eternal punishment for a single minor sin is impossible.

Core Idea
Eternal punishment for one sin violates Mu'tazilite justice.

This lesson examines a proof that turns the Mu'tazilite principle of divine justice against itself. The author presents a scenario where a person of lifelong faith commits one minor sin, and argues that eternal punishment would be unjust even by Mu'tazilite standards. The passage uses a reductio ad absurdum to force the conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full translation. Notice the scenario described.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the scenario and the principle
The passage describes a person who maintains faith and good deeds for a hundred years, then commits one minor sin (like drinking a sip of wine). Identify the principle: 'it is not appropriate from the Wise One' (لا يحسن من الحكيم).
This builds on the Mu'tazilite concept of divine justice.
3
Understand the reductio argument
The author concludes that if this scenario is not considered injustice (ظلم) or blameworthy (ذم), then nothing would be. This is a reductio that forces the opponent to accept the conclusion that eternal punishment for such a sin is unjust.
This argument is effective because it uses the Mu'tazilite's own premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث - وهو على قاعدة الاعتزال، أن من واظب على الإيمان والعمل الصالح مائة سنة، وصدر عنه في أثناء ذلك أو بعده جريمة واحدة كشرب جرعة من الخمر، فلا يحسن من الحكيم أن يعذبه على ذلك أبد الآباد. ولو لم يكن هذا ظلماً ، فلا ظلم ، أو لم يستحق بهذا ذماً، فلا ذم .
Third—and it is based on the principle of Mu'tazilism, that whoever perseveres in faith and righteous deeds for a hundred years, and then there issues from him during that or afterwards a single crime like drinking a sip of wine, it is not appropriate from the Wise One to punish him for that forever and ever. If this is not injustice, then nothing is injustice; or if this does not deserve blame, then nothing deserves blame.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that draws on the Mu'tazilite's own concept of divine justice (على قاعدة الاعتزال). The author argues by example: if a person maintains faith and good deeds for a century, then commits a single sin like drinking a small amount of wine, it is inconceivable (لا يحسن) for a wise and just God to punish that person eternally (أبد الآباد). The argument is that such a disproportionate punishment would violate justice. The author clinches with a reductio: if this is not considered injustice (ظلم) or blameworthy (ذم), then nothing would be. This argument is particularly effective against the Mu'tazilites who emphasize divine justice as a core principle.

Key Terms
قاعدة الاعتزال
الظلم
الذم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument only works for Ash'aris.
Correction: The author explicitly builds the argument 'on the principle of Mu'tazilism' (على قاعدة الاعتزال), using the Mu'tazilites' own standards of justice against them.

Checkpoint
On which group's principle does the third proof rely to argue against eternal punishment for a single sin?
A) The Ash'aris
B) The Mu'tazilites
C) The Kharijites
D) The Jahmites

Key Takeaway
The author uses the Mu'tazilite's own standard of divine justice to show that eternal punishment for a minor sin is unjust and therefore impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were the person in the example—a hundred years of faith and good deeds, then one slip—would you feel that eternal punishment is just? What does your answer reveal about how you understand God's attribute of justice?
?
The author uses a 'sip of wine' as a trivial sin to expose the absurdity of disproportionate punishment. Consider your own view of small sins: do you treat them as insignificant? How does this argument challenge you to take every sin seriously while also trusting in God's perfect justice?
?
Imagine standing before God with a lifetime of worship and a single hidden sin. Would you be confident in God's justice to be fair, or would you beg for mercy? How does this passage reshape your reliance on God's attributes beyond just His justice?

Fourth Proof: Finite Punishment for Finite Sin
Argues for finite punishment based on sin's finitude, contrasts with kufr, and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof that punishment for sins other than kufr must be finite, based on the finitude of sin in time and degree, and how the author refutes the objection about eternal punishment.

Core Idea
Sin is finite in time and degree; its punishment must be finite, unlike kufr which is infinite in degree.

This lesson examines the fourth proof in the text, which argues for proportional justice: finite sin deserves finite punishment. The author distinguishes sin from disbelief (kufr) and addresses a potential objection regarding eternal punishment. You'll see how the argument relies on a clear rational principle and a careful analysis of degrees of punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the logical flow: the claim, its justification, the contrast with kufr, and the objection-response.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two aspects of finitude
The author states that sin is finite in time and in degree. Understand how each aspect supports the conclusion that punishment must be finite.
Finitude in degree means there exist worse sins; thus the sin is not the worst possible.
3
Understand the distinction from kufr
Note how kufr is different: it is infinite in degree even if finite in time. That justifies eternal punishment for kufr but not for lesser sins.
This distinction is key to the proof.
4
Examine the objection and response
The author considers the objection that eternal punishment is the most severe and thus only for the worst crime (kufr). The response: punishment levels can vary in intensity even if duration is the same.
This shows that eternal punishment for sins could be less intense than for kufr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع - أن المعصية متناهية زماناً ، وهو ظاهر وقدراً لما يوجد من معصية أشد منها فجزاؤها يجب أن يكون متناهياً تحقيقاً لقاعدة العدل بخلاف الكفر، فإنه لا يتناهى قدراً، وإن تناهى زمانه . وأما التمسك بأن الخلود في النار أشد العذاب وقد جعل جزاء لأشد الجنايات - وهو الكفر - فلا يصح جعله جزاء بما هو دونه كالمعاصي . فربما يدفع بتفاوت مراتب العذاب في الشدة، وإن تساوت في عدم الانقطاع .
Fourth—that sin is finite in time, which is apparent, and in degree, because there exists a sin more severe than it, so its punishment must be finite to achieve the principle of justice, unlike disbelief (kufr), for it is not finite in degree, even if finite in time. As for clinging to the claim that eternity in hell is the most severe punishment and has been made the recompense for the most severe crimes—that is, disbelief—it is not correct to make it the recompense for what is less than that, namely sins. Perhaps it is repelled by the variation of levels of punishment in severity, even if they are equal in lack of cessation.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof based on proportionality of punishment. The author argues that every sin (ma'siya) besides disbelief (kufr) is finite (متناهية) in two respects: time (it occupies a limited period) and degree (there exist sins worse than it). Therefore, the punishment for such sins must also be finite to uphold justice. This contrasts with kufr, which is infinite in degree (لا يتناهى قدراً) even if its time is finite. The author then addresses a potential objection: one might argue that eternal punishment (khulud) is the most severe punishment and is reserved for the worst crime—kufr—so it cannot be applied to lesser sins. The author responds that even if the duration is infinite, the levels of intensity within that punishment can vary (تفاوت مراتب العذاب في الشدة). Thus, sinners could be punished eternally but with a less severe torment than disbelievers. This counters the objection by allowing differentiation within eternal punishment.

Key Terms
متناهية
الكفر
خلود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument implies all sins deserve equal punishment (eternal or not).
Correction: The author explicitly distinguishes between kufr and lesser sins in degree, and allows for differentiation in severity even if punishment is eternal, so the argument does not imply equal punishment.

Checkpoint
In what ways does the author say sin (ma'siya) is finite?
A) Only in time
B) Only in degree
C) In both time and degree
D) Neither in time nor degree

Key Takeaway
Sin's finitude in time and degree demands a finite punishment, but the possibility of varying intensity allows for eternal punishment of lesser intensity for sins different from kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a sin you committed that you consider 'small.' Does this lesson allow you to dismiss it as insignificant? What does the finitude of that sin demand from you in terms of repentance and accountability? Will you take a concrete step today to seek forgiveness for it?
?
If kufr is the only sin infinite in degree, have you ever examined your own heart for traces of disbelief—arrogance, ingratitude, or neglect of Allah's signs? What would it mean for you if your 'minor' neglect of faith actually borders on kufr? How will you actively strengthen your iman this week?
?
The argument admits that eternal punishment can vary in intensity. Does that comfort you or frighten you? Comfort, because God's justice is precise; or frighten, because even the 'lightest' eternal torment is unimaginable. Let this push you to take every sin seriously, no matter how finite it seems. What is one habit you will change starting today?
